Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, apply cautery on the joint, one cautery on each joint, and two small cauteries on the stomach in addition to the large one, because the cure is beneficial where there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure for hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When the hemorrhoids are founded, either one or more, and they are old and are of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and they are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not help if cauteries are made: .iij. above the spine of the back, that which is completely turned away from almecdate hole by hole and triangular, and .i. cautery below the anus. 2 dois;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the charnositeit which is named "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you apply the cautery to althelul, heat up the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it completely on top of the althelul being cut; and leave your hand so that the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, thus cutting the vein; do this once or twice, and if there is much althelul, cauterize each one as we have said; afterwards, use the healing balm until it heals completely; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the alchatim, it will provide more aid.
de plaie mal curee	from an improperly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	If the patient cannot bear incision or opening, which we will explain in its place, this disease comes that can only be healed by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	1. When any abscess comes, and it becomes swollen and corrupted due to moisture, one must examine the whole situation carefully and know how deep the abscess has penetrated.
de la maladie des reins	on the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of cold comes to the kidneys and with large swelling, and it does not take in women, then you must perform cautery on both sides of the kidneys using the cautery claw that we have mentioned earlier; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be four cauteries in a row, and it will provide more significant aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold or moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery in the area outside of the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on each side, and both should be as long as the knuckle; and make one cautery outside the back, or two if needed; and let the cauterization be clavicle-shaped according to the previously mentioned form.
de la marris	of the anus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the anus is cold and moist, and cannot conceive, and the flowers (semen) are corrupted and their term ends late; and when they come, it causes great pain: then it must be done to him four cauteries around the buttocks, as we have said in the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauteries outside the back; and let the cauterization be clavicle-shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the hernia
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous hernias descend into the belly of the hernia, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the signs are that the leg is longer than the other when measured together; and the location of the hernia can be seen visually in the area of protrusion; if so, you must cauterize the patient over the belly of the hernia with a cautery resembling a circle and sign before the hernia, as it turns, so that the hernia is within the circle; and if the cauterizing is like those who have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available to you, make four large olive-oil cauterizes, and make sure the cauteries are as deep as all the others; and cure it until it heals.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hernia
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the swelling of the hernia, and it is due to coldness and moisture; the patient is treated as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not work, and the disease is ancient: therefore you must purge the patient of the gross humors with fetid pills or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that, perform the cautery; and the method of the cautery is according to two methods: either with burning substances mixed with medicines or cauterization by fire. Cauterization by fire is according to many ways, one of which is as follows: you should cauterize on top of the swelling of the hernia four triangular cauteries according to this shape (see figure), and make it deep and large, with a space of the thickness of a die between each cautery. The cauteries should be made of olive oil; sometimes they are performed in the middle on the head of the hernia, for which there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, if you cauterize the cautery of the circular shape which we have mentioned earlier in dislocation of the shoulder; but do it in such a manner that the circles encompass the entire shoulder, and all the edges of the cavity are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the way it's done for sciatica, when the pain remains in the shoulder and does not reach down to the thigh or leg. If it reaches down to the thigh and leg, two cauteries are performed where the patient says that the pain is located, and one cautery above the ankle .5 inches, on the left side a little bit; and let the cauteries be cutlery type, and burn the thickness of the cavity; if the patient feels that the pain extends to toes or close to it, cauterize where they feel pain 3-4 points or 4 at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if you know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with a cutlery or circular cauterizer, and take great care in all your cauteries not to burn the nerves and large arteries, and avoid causing greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who performed cautery on the foot of the leg, and they let it swell completely, both the legs and the feet, and all the toes were pierced and corrupted. After a stomach solution from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places together, perform cautery on one and the other, according to this method. // The wise will say in the cautery of the hip, as follows: Make a rod of iron that is as thick as a nail of the thumb or slightly less, and let it be between-the-cheeks (i.e., transversely) or from one between-the-cheek to the other of a space equal in size to a nut of the index finger; and the between-the-cheeks should be 2 fingers apart, and they should be round, and it should have one iron handle well made; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Let it be heated until it is completely red and scalded with hot irons, then place it on the sick person's hipboast (a term used to denote the iliac crest) and turn it towards the healthy side; and cauterize once with a hot iron and let it rest for 4 days; then apply an ointment of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery sparingly due to the fear of its sight, and few do so who employ it; however, this is one of the good cauteries which can endure it, and where it is used.
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either by falling or impact or excessive evacuation, or from similar causes of cold matter spreading, none of these resemble cauteries unless for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is required after this that the patient is emptied of fetid pills or similar things, which are placed on the back where the pain is, three lines signed with ink, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the power and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cautery should be made according to the cautery which is called "poins"; and if you see, make four cauteries or four at the middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow anus when they defecate, and fear; and you will find it in the lower spine of the back and in its appearance which comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	The cautery should increase each part of the spine. And if you see, cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointing .2 or .3 lines, and the points should be close to each other. Afterwards, cure the area until it is healthy, as we have said; but take care not to apply the cautery in a gillyblister that is near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain in the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain in the joints is due to moisture that spreads to every member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which people call "podagra" properly, and when it is from cold causes and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this way: make the mould for the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary that you press on the thigh bone, make a fire cautery over its entire length as they claim "point". And if pains come up to the joints and this often happens, make a fire cautery on each thigh for four or three times on each part, using an olive oil cautery; and if more is needed, do it again, but don't hold your hand outside for longer than the flesh burns.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	If pains reach the thighs and back, administer the cautery as described in our chapter. If pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist lines; if there is no pain left in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, take good care of the patient and think about medicines. For if you take good care of him and purge the fluid, he will be cured with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the hernia
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When hernia comes in anger, and the bulge descends towards the groin and this is new, it should be noted that when you wish to cure it, it must not eat anything that day; and it should use things which ease the stomach, so that the feces descend from the stomach. After doing so, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to pull his arm as far as possible towards the affected side, and then take hold of the bulge with both hands, and press firmly over the hernia above the bone of the little finger, and at a certain sign that is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery in the shape specified below:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then straighten out the bulges to their place; and the minister holds his hand where they do not return; and work well on the patient's thighs, and put one cushion and one belt under him on the thighs, and another one across the affected area that holds his hands; then place the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and hold it straight and until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the bulge does not swell while you apply the cautery; and do not burn it; and in this way, may the patient not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. The cauteries for children should be subtle according to their size, and those for adults as large according to their size; after three days, cure the wound caused by the cautery with butter until the burn is healed; after that, treat it with other ointments until it is healthy, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his excretions be relaxed for a long time, so that the bulge does not swell when he gets up to go to the chamber.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, offer him a well-made bandage and keep it for forty more days; let him have good rest, that he should work little and take care of not overfilling with drinking and eating, and not letting out too much urine; and when he does this teaching, then he will be completely cured. And I shall say afterwards the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the wound from the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds appear in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they are not growing more, make one cautery of cautery according to its size, and burn the third part of the fat; afterwards cure according to what we have said; and no one of the ancients has said that it should be cauterized at four angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But first, make a mark at the joint and draw a line above the incision, and another below it, and place your hand on the entire fire-cautery. However, the first cauterizations are lighter and more mobile.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any member, either from a fall or an injury, and that pain lasts long, and the medicine does not cure it, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, strength, and location of twists and pain. If the first cauterization is healthy, that's good; if not, repeat another cauterization on it, for it is customary that it changes in the nearby member, so you must make the cauteries as long as the patient remains unhealthy.
de meselerie	To mix or compound (medicines)
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The cauteries are sometimes used to aid in mixing or compounding (medicines), and especially the patient who comes from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. If you see it being cauterized, take care that the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and neither dissolves nor remains, and you doubt that corruption will affect the entire patient, then perform five cauteries on the head: one on the forehead near the hairline, two on the temples, one behind the ears, and one on the nose, leaving your hand long enough for the cautery to reach the bone, and so that scorches come out, allowing vapors of the gross humors to escape; and cauterize on the mice as necessary.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is scattered everywhere, it clearly perishes, then you must cauterize with the cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery on the nape of the neck, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the crotch and another opposite it, and two on each shoulder; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the ankles, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; beware of the nerves that are near the last calcant, do not burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the finger, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more you perform cauterization, the more help it provides and benefits the patient; and know that the sick do not feel pain from cauterization as the healthy do, because the body is already completely corrupted. And it is necessary that the cautery should be large or small according to the members and joints, as you will find in manuals of ironwork. Afterward, clean the site with flour several times with honey and other treatments until it heals.
de enfleure	Know that by prolonged application of leeches, there is greater benefit; and know that the sick do not feel pain from the leeches as the healthy do, because the body is already completely corrupted. And it is necessary to apply the leeches according to the size of the affected area and the type of wound, as you will find in manuals on leeching. Afterward, clean the site with saltwater several times until it heals.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When a swelling appears in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but does not heal, then you perform cauterization on the affected limb according to its size and smallness; and the cautery should be about the thickness of a finger. Then cure it with ointments until it heals. Sometimes one performs cauterization at the hand, foot, or back, at the nerve endings that immobilize the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; but no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about members and the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	Of swabs (or bandages)
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" occurs and the medical devices have no effect on it, then cauterize with a shallow cautery of a certain size according to the thickness of the skin, until the blister is removed and its color changes; then cure with flour and lentils mixed with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood from colon and almonds, of each one part; and mix everything together, tie it up with a cloth, and apply it to the place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	They cure scrofula (scrofula is a term for a chronic skin disease, often associated with tuberculosis) through cautery.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the abscess begins and you wish to stop it, cauterize with the cautery that appears like a circle around the abscess. And although the wise say to cauterize also in the middle of the abscess; and though this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen once; and a more proper thing is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circular", as we have said about cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	The inflammation which cannot move
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays healing due to the excess that it causes or due to the age of the patient when he is decrepit (meaning very old) and has little blood, or because of the time; and you wish to hasten its healing: then cauterize it with small cauteries all around, pricking; afterwards leave it in this state. For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced through entirely with the fire cautery, heat the cautery as follows:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Keep your hand in the midst of that disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and make the cautery such that the patient feels it moving through in this manner so that the course of the purgation is clear. Afterwards, cure it completely when it is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	treatment with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of disease it has, which is called "corrodens", and nothing else but an eating away of the limbs, for it eats the limbs just as fire dries out damp wood. If you see this disease in a place that can be cauterized with fire along with heat, then heat the cautery small and large according to where the disease is; after the cauterization of all parts until you eradicate all corruption, and nothing remains of it, cut out everything corrupted. And leave it for 3 days, and put soft ointment made from crushed cauterized pieces with oil on the burned areas until the burns due to fire are healed, and all the corruption. After the cure by ointments generates char, or if after 3 days, char is not healthy, then repeat the cauterization on the remaining corrupted parts. And this eating away is sometimes cured with medicine for ague instead of cauterization with fire; but nevertheless, cauterization of fire is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure for ague in the division: take it as needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The hairs which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Frequently, a disease called "clos" arises in the feet according to our understanding, and it is a large thing that scalds the foot. And the cauteries for this disease are in two ways. This includes cautery by fire, and cautery by hot water. Cautery by fire means heating one cautery comb as is a feather of a quill, made of good iron to the size that it can pierce the nail of all parts, and there should be narrow margins; place it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it comes out at the font of the nail; and leave it thus for four days until it begins to discharge pus; then make a poultice of evil herbs ground with oil, and leave the poultice on top of it all night, and the nails will shrink and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the wound with healing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if it is turned inside the body (by external injury), and this frequently happens in hands and feet, you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done in this manner: take a cane made of iron or quill, and place it on the nail and the blisters (boils); then put the cane on top so that it encompasses all around, then place a small amount of hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the margins of the cane reach the root of the nail, and let the hot water find its way through to the root; and let the patient endure a little bit of the hot water for an hour; then leave it as it is, and it will be uprooted from all its roots. Do this repeatedly until you have treated all the injuries in the body, and then cure them with healing ointments that promote healing.
li cure dou trembler	The cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	For some who tremble from cold or nerves, or from quartan fever, or something else, it is necessary that you make four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one between each spine; and one at the shin, and one on the stomach with olive oil cautery; this will stop the trembling, and the healthiness will depart from the illness.
des pustules puans	of putrid boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes the body is affected by swellings that are putrid boils due to decaying large matter. In the first instance when they appear, it is necessary to make a cautery on each of the heads of the pustule: one with fine wire from myrtle wood, which should be inserted in the fire or with long root of aristolochia or cauterizing lenticular. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, according to this method, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluous matter from them is discharged, and they become healthy; however, it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great discharges of blood from the cut artery at the wound that comes out to the exterior, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cautery of a limb, and similar things; it is a very grave thing to let it drain out.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And in all cases, when it happens, quickly put your finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it very firmly until the blood is stopped from flowing out; then take smaller and larger olive oil cauteries and heat them all to red; then take .i., whether large or small depending on the wound and the location in which the artery is located, and place the cautery on that vein where you have your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped from flowing.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a jump occurs when you place your finger on the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take quickly another one of the cauteries that are near the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing one after the other until the vein is completely sealed; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is exposed, and avoid any other harm coming to the patient; and know that when blood stops flowing from the artery, it cannot be properly restrained if it is not through one of the four methods that we have mentioned: either by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by tightly tying thread, or by medicines placed on it which have the power to stop blood; and tie and hold it accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies tight bandages or places hot substances on it, or similar things, will not benefit if the above method does not help.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has no remedy or medicine present, then you should place your finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it out until it is held in place above the wound and above the vein; and do not move it, but the cold moisture should be often applied that is very cold so that the blood remains congealed and thickened and held in place; and proceed with the investigation of the one in need of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have already told you in the first chapter about all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or hot medicine, and we discussed their origins, instruments, forms of cauteries; and I placed that chapter on the head down to the feet, and I will continue in this chapter in the same way so that those things which are more easily found can be understood.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauterizations, and for this reason greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to undertake foolishness. For many kinds of people come to be treated. Some come in such a state with their disease that they die quickly due to the insanity caused by their illness, and from the great cruelty of their condition; and one should fear this.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And from these who give you counsel and say: "Wait, I am healed"; the patient is arrogant. You should not readily agree to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more importance on your honor than on your desire, and be careful rather than rash in what you are certain of, and from which you can take and learn; and use prediction and indication in healing your patients so that salvation is attained; and this will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and lasting praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dearest son, may our Lords grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Moreover, I have organized this chapter in discussing by chapters, according to what is before the chapter of cauteries, which I have previously discussed from head to feet, because you will find it easier to understand those things that you may need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often comes to children during childbirth, and sometimes it happens for reasons unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone other than children, and for all those I have seen, death was swift; therefore, it seems to me that it is worthwhile to seek out remedies in various treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw an infant whose head was swollen with water, and it grew larger each day until it could no longer support it; and the moisture gathered under the bone above the siphatic, between the brain and the bone; and the procedure is such that if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make an incision in the head a wide opening; and let it be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture can flow out; and here is the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscesses are larger, make two incisions in the form of a cross, as follows:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the signs that I show, the incisions where the head parts are open, and when you press it from inside with your hand, it does not respond; then you should make four incisions in the head as follows:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision remove all the moisture entirely. Then close the wounds with bandages and powders, put vinegar and oil on it and let it be until the fifth day; then undress it, and treat the wound with lints and ointments, and allow the swelling to subside, and give the patient dry meat from a boar as much as needed while the member is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is to observe where the abscess is largest, and assemble the pus; because sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, cut where the abscess opens, and collect the pus, and make an incision accordingly as you can; but be careful not to cover the artery; and let blood flow out so that the patient may die in a proper manner from the loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When a disease called "catarrh" affects any of the eyes or at its worst, and the disease is old, and the medicine's cure does not help at all, then the last cure is the cautery with which two arteries will be touched.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you wish to cover the arteries, let the patient bend his head back; afterwards rub the area of a rough cloth on him until the arteries appear, then tighten the patient's neck with one rough cloth; then look where the veins are located, and they are found behind the ears, and there they will be found; then mark the veins with a sign, then touch one and the other with a sharp spatula of 2 inches until the cut reaches the bone, and this should be done wide around the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see (it), push the spatula beneath the artery and strike it from above, cutting as deeply as two fingers' width.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is cut, it jumps out without ceasing continuously upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open by itself, then you must measure the width of three fingers, then dig deeply until you reach the bone; and the amount of blood that needs to be released is 7 cubic centimeters, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure and the fullness of the artery. Then observe the wound: if it remains above the bone without being siphoned off, then do not open the abscess as you have prescribed, but hold the wound and bind it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	From migration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old migraine comes with a sharp catarrh, due to moisture in the eyes and heat in the temples and ancient forsenee and similar things, and it is treated with medicines and cures, but none of them help, we should cut open the arteries of the temples and cauterize, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient should bend down the hair on his temples, and listen to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well due to its beating, and can be found easily except in some cold men; and if it is found, the patient should pull out the neck of the artery with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and wet the place with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula as follows:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then gently scrape the skin to reveal the artery, then pull it up towards the pulse-takes (pinceures), and remove carefully the cords that are beneath each part; and if the artery is delicate, turn it at the tip of the unguis (uncine). Then chop off that part according to the size of the two shoulders (chiés). For if it's not chopped, it will not move at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	Then draw out the blood from the vein for six inches, and if the artery is large, you should tie it with a double strong silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound of the incision, and there is continuous flow of blood; then chop off the excess between the two cords at that hour itself, and if you see, then cauterize the cautery with the knife to the bone until the shoulders are chopped; this work is performed when the patient does not have fever and he has a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauteries are helpful for ending moisters: because it is of greater aid to moisters.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	1. In the extraction of arteries, one should fill the area with old cotton and place well-made tweezers on top; and when you pull them apart, heal it with dry medicines that cause heat, and with tweezers, until it is healed; and if there is no incision in the artery as you work, hastily cover it with cautery, or use vitriol and hold your hand on it to stop the bleeding; and if you don't have that available, place your finger on the area until it stops bleeding, and freeze the area with cold water frequently, and hold it as needed; and the more tender and lighter in the extraction of the artery is, the more you should cauterize the vein of this sharp cautery, but the incision should be thick to keep its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have one fingerbreadth of space between the two blades, and then when you have signed both leagues, and heat the iron until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two leagues; and they should be spaced apart because the cautery is not welded to the entire thing throughout; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	Tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes run down the veins that are above the head of the fire, and no medicine cure helps it, and you see the patient wrinkle his face and feel feverish like shivers; and if they are tender and moist so that the hair on the scalp falls out, and the eyebrows are scalded and burned by the tears, this requires this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called it the "contused cure" in ancient times, and you should make incisions on the patient's forehead where he has hair, then make four equal cuts along the length of the forehead; one cut should be as deep as two fingers moving downward from the forehead, and the other two cuts should be at .ii. costelz above the eyebrows, but take care not to cut the arteries that are at the .ii. costelz above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the .ii. mandibules, and each incision should be the size of 4 fingers joined together.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And prepare a piece of sponge and much cloth for wiping the blood, then insert the sharp spatula two fingers' breadth from this shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is above the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the cartilage that is between the two cuts along the bone, then do the other side from the middle incision to the second one, and then pull out this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	insert the instrument called "culter" (which is pointed on one side and soft, not pointed, and its shape is:)
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the cut edge towards the raw flesh at the discretion, and the cut should be soft towards the bone, and press it until it reaches the mid-incision. And cut all the veins that descend from the head to the eyes while the incision is continuous up to where the skin opens, and then make another incision in the mid-incision towards the other side; and then equalize the bleeding, and express the juices for the blood taken; then put a piece of old cotton cloth into each incision, and put damp linen soaked in wine and oil and ashes on top, and ensure that no pus enters it; on the third day, untie the ligature, and apply a large amount of strong vinegar, then the cure of ointment with basilicon and oil, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	the removal of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a person comes with an acute catarrh, you usually see soft and small eyes, and the vision is dimmed, and burned paper particles; hairs fall out, and the head throbs in pain, and the patient coughs; then know by these signs that those substances and this catarrh do not come from anywhere else but from many veins, and the remedy for it, if there is one, is to cure the veins.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And instruct the patient to bend their head backwards, then make a large cut across the forehead and another wide one. Begin from the temple on the left side to the temple on the right side, and let the incision reach the bone; and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating; when the bone is exposed, drain all the blood onto a sponge, then press between the two lips of the cut and place old cotton, and bind it with linen; then cover it with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil, and be careful not to cause an abscess to heat up; when removed, you must rub the bone until char begins to grow, then treat it with things that encourage char growth.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	Take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony and make a plaster with it; administer it to these wounds to encourage char growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of ears (blockage or congestion)
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, beasts, stones or similar things such as iron; seeds, such as peas, beans, and lentils; or flowing substances like water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	If a stone or anything else falls into the ear and does not fit in the ear or grow in the ear, put the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, pour some purple oil or camphor oil on it, then bring extraction; and make him vomit from condisci, and stop his nostrils when vomiting comes, and place pieces of fabric or wool around the ear; and hold the ear above. Often times farting comes with this cure; and if it does not fart, bring extraction with fine tweezers as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it farts with tweezers, that's good; if not, bring extraction with a fine thin hook; and if it does not fart with this, make a cane of beeswax and push the head of the cane or the hole of the ear forcefully, and stop the area around the cane with molten wax so that air cannot enter with the cane; then pull it out carefully, as often times it will fart in this way; and if it does not fart in this manner, take glue from where you get it, put it on any instrument that is sharp for this purpose, put some cotton around it; then press the glue against the stone or whatever it may be and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump out of all these things that we have said, then you must hurry to cut the ear before abscess pus comes and spasms; and the method of cutting is that you first anesthetize the patient with the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to the measure of its power, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut in the root of the ear where the fat or the meat hangs; and let the cut be like a moon, until you reach the bone, then break it as best as you can, and suck quickly with your mouth; and the cure lasts until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is pus that is swelling, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer one thin, subtle sponge according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and make an incision of that pus. But do not do it when you think the pus is moist because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with fine tweezers and a sucker, as we have said, so that the extraction is even.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the water that falls into the ear, instruct the patient to use warm condiments first and fill the ear with soft cotton. Let the patient lie on the affected ear. If it jumps out due to this, that's good. If not, take many small and light pebbles according to the size of your finger, heat them slightly in fire; then insert one or two of these heated pebbles into the ear, and place another stone on top of the one in the ear; do not stop heating the other pebble with fire until the water completely jumps out, making it jump out entirely; and if you see, take a feather, and press one of the stones in the ear, while holding the other head with fire until the larger stone is burned; then repeat this process with other pebbles until the water completely comes out, as we have said before.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of animals, if it is small like fleas and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is large that can be felt, introduce tweezers for extraction; and it is easier to remove whatever is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the removal of parasitic worms from the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and use distillation methods, and the cure does not help; if you observe no worms, take a piece of this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And let it be narrow below and wide above. Push the most subtle head into the ear according to the degree of pain of the patient, then squeeze firmly all the way along the cane; do this often until all the worms come out. If they do not obey to come out, stop up around the cane with cotton as I have said before; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proved in the treatment of worms, and you will find them or treat the distillations there; and if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear to this extent, it is the form as you see:
