Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	Let it be made with silver or tin narrowly to a small opening, and above wide for distillation; and for pressing the distillate into one instrument of tin well made for this purpose, take one scraper and wrap around its point with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you choose from your medicines into the cane, and let it be in the ear; then push the scraper into the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or turned over in the ear; and the patient should smell the scent inside, and the distillate should be heated with a small flame as if you were distilling it in the ear; but make sure it's not too cold, for the medicine will not be effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear stoppage (stopping/blockage of the ears)
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any ear defects; and this same thing happens in men due to an injury of the ear, or pus born within the ear, and this injury sometimes goes all the way into the ear, if one cannot see it; and sometimes it only affects one side of the ear, and one can clearly see it.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, if it goes all the way into the ear and cannot be seen, it is grave treatment in many conditions, and in that case you must put the diseased ear in the sun and look inside: if you see the pus appearing, then open it with this spatula as shown here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be careful to make it sharp both in front and behind so that it does not pierce the ear; if the pus is from pus or flesh of the ear, then hold the tweezers subtly and gently remove it until all the pus is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the swelling is deep in the ear, take a subtle sharp instrument and heat it slightly over fire, then place it into the ear canal. If you feel the swelling, as the patient feels pain in hearing, make a small incision gently, ensuring not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a linen patch according to the size of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Keep the dressing moist with rose water and powdered vitriol for each day until the wound is healed. If you see the ear swell up, it is necessary to remove the dressing and replace it with another moistened dressing made of rose oil and beeswax until the swelling goes down; then treat it until it becomes healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, then place it on the ear, and use other treatments to stop the bleeding which are either cauterization or distillation treatments.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of paper (meaning "skin")
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is a remedy for hair that comes from the skin when it is moist and dry; you should stretch them with tongs and tweezers, and strike at their roots with a spatula; then apply powdered vitriol to the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it cannot be plucked out (the hair), then cauterize with the subtle cautery of lentil seeds, and cauterizing after incision is useful; and many times they heal, because nothing remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, the roots burn away and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the hail (meaning "hardened lumps under the skin")
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Often in paper come out some things that resemble hail in shape and hardness, and for this reason is the disease called "grandine", and it is a thick mass of moisture on top and underneath the paper; the treatments are as follows: take care to ensure the grandine becomes silent from both sides, which is an easy thing to know; then make a large opening, gently peel each side, then grasp with pliers and crush. If you cannot crush it without piercing the paper, do not worry the patient; if the tear is large, assemble it with stitches, and care for it until it heals; if it is small, do not apply force, because oil restores it soon and causes harm.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	If the grandine descends inside the ear towards the upper part, invert the paper, grasp the grandine with pliers and crush it and press from both sides; if the paper is pushed back by the incision, do not worry; when the grandine is crushed, apply saltwater oil and care for the area that causes harm until the patient heals.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a grease that is impregnated in cloths made of paper above, and this happens more often in infants than in adults, and it greatly irritates their eyes, and they wake up with catarrh at mornings, and cannot endure the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; and therefore, they lie on their faces immediately, sleep on top, and their paper cloths are moist under their eyelids that the exinach spreads in the oil. And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places their head on a clean surface; then take one linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach from each part, then place it over; press with your hands on either side so that the exinach is enclosed within the circle; then make a slit in the center of the moistener with a sharp lancet, but not larger than the wound made for venesection; and cut the skin completely until you see the exinach; and from various positions comes exinach from the incision, according to the form of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take a piece of coarse cloth between your hands and turn your hand to the left and right until it is spread; and ensure that you do not stray in the incision, that you come entirely to the oil, that you do not pierce it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not open at the beginning of the cut, lift a little on the cut lightly until it opens; then pull out as we have said, then moisten cloths in oil and vinegar, and place it on the wound, and hold bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And to those who grind oil and place it over to corrupt the moisture that has remained. Then heal it until it is healed. If an abscess arises hot at the site, treat with plasters soothing it until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	hair from paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like growths grow on the eyelids other than nature, and are nourished, they harm the eyes, and cause diseases such as customary tears and swelling of the paper-like growths, until it leads to the destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways of cure: either by cautery with fire, or by medicine for ague according to what is mentioned in the previous chapter on cautery, or by incision and stitching, or by caustics, as I shall explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper-like growth on the eye towards your left hand; if it is reversed, that is good; if not, poke an awl with one thread over it; and cut off the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow from these hairs, and pull one thread along the entire length of the paper, then shave it; then make a hole in the part below the paper, under the hair-like growths, all the way from the great tear to the small one; then pull out one thread, and place a small tent made of cotton and linen under the paper, then sew a figure similar to the comb of the blackberry bush, and regardless of its shape, it must be according to the quantity that you see needs to lift the paper which is designated for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a need to remove a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper has become softened; then you make an incision on all the lines that you have marked, starting from the great tear to the small one; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs, then insert the hook in one of the two angles of the cut, then scrape it all out; then bring the two lips together with a stitch made with an awl and a thread of fine linen, and squeeze out the blood, and make it adhere to any sticky substances, if you wish to do so; but if not, leave the stitches and wait for 2 or 3 days before curing the wound without stitches using drying and constricting agents, as the paper will reattach itself at the edge of the wound and by its assembly, but the stitches will rot (as the ancients say), and this is laborious work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And in another way, you shall fold the paper into a shape like the fennel of myrtle, as we have said, three times according to the form shown below:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then fold what is above the small areas equally according to the shape shown below:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the pliers and the parts are not equal, take a needle with one thread and place it in the figure; put another thread from the large armhole, and the second thread from the small, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin that you have marked, as we have said; then sew together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes the hair of the paper turns: it is necessary that you use what has been said about incision; but stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of wounds is as follows: and it is that you fold the paper and place it inside according to what I have said, and then make two stitches by hand, and two thin threads equally long as the paper and the thickness of the spatula; take hold of the two corners with these threads; next, bring the two stitched parts together subtly over the top of the folded paper covered by oil, and bind the two stitches from the two sides together; leave it for some days, and the skin that is being bound will die, rot, and fall off, leaving the wound open.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long and you must forcefully apply the remedy, cure it until it is healed; when the wound is healed and the paper can be removed, and no more hair will grow; this is the form of the two stitches that you will make according to this figure and this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The operations are such that you take a fine needle, and insert one silk thread of the same fineness; then bring the heads together delicately, and let the length of the threads be about a palm's length; then assemble another fine silk thread briefly, tie the ends of the thread; then put the patient's head in your lap; and expose the operations to the sun so that they are visible, for it is a delicate and small operation, then pierce the needle through the entire chase in the root of the hair adjacent, and make it pass quickly through the skin until you pull it over the natural hair; then remove the hair up to the chase, and insert the removed hair into the chase if there is one or two or three or more; then stretch your hand so that the hairs come out from under the chase with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull the chase away to where the thread you ordered has been placed, so that the chase comes out through the hole and can be seen by oil vision; then you will pull the chase and the thread, close the wound and the opening, and leave it for 2 or 3 days, until the hair adheres in its place and new flesh grows; if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from natural growth, and let it grow with that one until it is elongated and then clean it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or corruption comes in oil, there are two kinds: natural and unnatural. And it happens suddenly from a wound, or a cut or burn, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way of working with it is to split that suture, separate its lips, put dampened flax within, and leave it until it heals; and you must not use anything in its treatment that dries or constricts. For if you do this, the disease returns worse than the first; but it works with things softening, such as fenugreek; and the decoction of water or ale and flax seeds should be cooked, and immediately cooled down into any oil, and wrap it in a cloth, and cure it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you keep it from healing in the same way as it was before; and this work we have said is not without remedy for this disease, so that it does not return in the same way as it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the chyle which comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is truly called "axacrati", and is both natural and accidental. The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cauterizations and similar things; and the procedure for this work is that you take a needle, in which there should be one double thread, and poke it into the chyle, starting from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads reach two heads of the chyle; then raise the chyle above the needle, and cover it with a .1-inch wide spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bone of the shoulder returns to its correct position, that is good; if not, take a rasp and place it in the gap, turn the bone, make two gaps where the bone is inside the shoulder; let the heads of the two bones from the two gaps be at the four angles of the incision you made, so that when they are assembled, the figure should be like the letter with the name "Y Greek"; then remove that cartilage, according to the amount it protrudes outside the bone, as a result of which the shoulder is; then join the two separated parts with a thread of linen; then treat with the medicines for softening and for drawing pus, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the illness comes from a cut or stitch or cautery, it is necessary to make a flat incision beneath the hairs of the shoulder, as described above; then separate between the two edges of a linen cloth, as I have said; and one should perform the operation according to the shape of the illness, because it is very different in shape, and wise masters prepare engines of all possible power to make the figure return to its natural form. The patient themselves, according to what is necessary for the operation and the application of instruments in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	the sudden dislocation of the shoulder
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens in the hands of men in such a way that the paper above is sealed with white oil and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor blade beneath the paper, lift it up; hold it with tweezers, until you grasp what is near the spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too deep so as not to cause pain to the patient because the spatula is too sharp and pierces the oil; and your incision, from which you scrape that assembly, should be light, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and the whole assembly heals, and sometimes there is infection in the sharp oil and leaching of sweet water and colic; then put a linen tent between the paper and the oil and place moist wool on top abundantly of egg; and after the third day use the colic and other healing things until it heals.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is of two kinds: one is nerve-like and resembles a hard horn, and another which is not nerve-like but resembles white frozen moisture; when it is touched by iron and boiled in tweezers, it cannot be moved; and both appear starting from the large root and grow little by little until it covers the entire eye and all light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient places his head in your hand, then you pull out the hairs; then take some paper in your hand, then pinch the nail with small tweezers, and extend it; then take a needle, and put on it a horse hair or cow hair or ox hair, and one strong thread; bend the tip of the needle slightly and poke it into the nail, pierce through it entirely, tie the nail with the thread, and extend it above; then scrape off all the skin surrounding the nail root, down to the flesh around it, including the gristle and sinew up to the head of the nail, then chop the remaining part in the root of the nail up to the quick, and scrape off all the subtle tissue and small forces, leaving only the natural flesh or root; and sometimes the nail should be extended only onto the onyx alone, and the thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the soft tissue surrounding it, as described in this form.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the tissue does not touch the flesh and break it, and that the gristle is not pierced; and after the incision pour oil a little amount of broken seed oil, and make a collyrium from litargirium, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with whatever is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerve-ridden and you cannot push the needle in, and the onions cannot enter, it is often cured with medicines for this kind of nail; and they grow as I mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, open the oil of the patient, and take a sharp spatula according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And the nail above shall be finely reamed, and if you see that it does not shrink at all and the reason persists, distill oil of collyrium made from litargyrium and red collyrium and crushed sulphur from your mouth into it; anoint the oil until the next day; then repeat the procedure according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing prevents you in the oil, as in the treatment of an abscess, first milk it, and heal the abscess hot until it is healed, then repeat the procedure as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the sore harms the oil greatly, suspend it at the onion and chop a part of it and not all, so that tears do not come from it; then distill into the oil collyrium red which is made of litargyrium.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	Of the flesh which grows upon the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	In some men, there sometimes grows red flesh upon the eyelid, covering it and pressing upon the lower and upper eyelids, resembling a rosebud of balustrade. And this happens when the patient puts their head in water, then they open the eyes, and all that red flesh should be cut off with scissors to the end, and you must take care not to wound the oil gland at the surgery; it is an incision like the spatula which we have mentioned in the incision of the nail and small forceps with which one extracts the seed, as the shape after this chapter shows.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, apply oil of seals crushed or distilled red collyrium resembling corrosive medicines, and place a piece of cotton with egg white on top to ensure that it stays warm; if anything remains, and the wound is not closed, and you doubt whether it is healed, leave the oil and heal the wound with things soothing a hot abscess; then return to your surgery until it is healthy, and do this every time red flesh grows in the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, you must treat each small wound with natural means; and for an accidental wound, in work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	These are red veins that are covered over the eye, and they perform their work and weaken the eye all day long. Therefore, it is necessary to first examine whether the eye, in which the red vein is, is healthy, and has no other disease except for the red vein; then treat it in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your hand, then press those veins all along according to your wisdom, and let the fingers be subtle and double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two points in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then make these veins subtle and gentle, and squeeze the blood out one after another, until you see them moving away from the oil; and be careful not to pierce the oil with the tips of the spatula-like instruments, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so as not to burn those veins; and when you have done that, if it distills green and red oil into a colander for correcting what is congealed within the blood.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect everything in that time, make a plaster on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and the abscess is certain to heal warmly, then continue as before until it is healthy again; and this is the form of the pressure:
de la fistule de l’oil	From the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The ulcer called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and burning medicine as I said earlier, and it is not healed, there is a trap in it that you cut open above the abscess where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, you will see the corruption and the blackness; if the joint is all the instrument as in this form; it is called "rough head", and it should be made straight by heating a rod of iron as shown here.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Place the exposed bone in your hand, then turn it between your palms and press your hand slightly until you know that the corruption is restored; do this once, then restore the position of healing herbs.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joint is swollen and pus forms, and the body of the bone is swollen, and remains in this state for forty days without changing or becoming abscessed, and any harmful accident does not occur (knowing it is healthy); if this is not so, there is no other remedy but to bring the fistula back to the wound as shown here: You should open the bone a second time with iron, with hot medicines, and when it is exposed, take a rod as shown here, which has four angles and the rod should be thin up to the head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone of the dislocated joint, and move your hand away from the oil (poc), then turn the whole tool (foret) all the way until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it if they hold their hand on their neck; and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have shown you, and when the flesh swells and hardens, the matter goes to the neck; it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the dislocation
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eyes are fully open and cannot be reduced or diminished in any way, you must tie the patient down; then clean the area with warm water, apply a plaster made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolle, and then secure it using bandages and cloths. The cloths should be soft enough that they can be folded four times and stacked one on top of the other according to the size needed; then secure them with a stiff bandage and renew the plasters without cutting to allow the area to heal. When the plaster has dissolved, remove it and if the eye is healing, it is good; if not, repeat the application of the plaster, cloths, and bandages until the eye heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The double rupture of the ruptured membrane.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the ruptured membrane, and fumigations come out like grains of resin, and it is frightening to see; then if you find it covered, the treatment is such that you thrust an awl into the root of the affected area from beneath up to where it is above, then another awl with a double thread from the edge of the tear; and make it pierce through, and leave the first awl according to its position; then tie the end of the double thread around the eye of the membrane and tighten it well, then withdraw the awl and apply soft oiled linen on top; and let it stay until the threads grow with the membrane, then heal the oil from healing substances as long as the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is held in place by the membrane from both sides of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show great appearance, pierce it with a fine spatula coming from oil, remove the white albugine and drain the eyes, then insert a probe immediately; then withdraw it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bowl of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not other than the swelling that forms in the eye, appearing like an eye-shaped ulcer but it is not an ulcer; and the manner of its appearance in the work is such that you make the patient sit on a flat and straight seat. Then take the head between your hands with two fingers, and move it until you see the swelling rise to your eyes; then pierce it, and let the light pass and let the patient see things as he usually does; and if it does not drain below, know that it is an ulcer, and if the drainage of the swelling is not prepared as we have said. Then make the patient sit between your hands, take the spatuline (a medical instrument) made of thin material and place it on the corneal membrane and the cornea, along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane and the cornea, until the swelling issues; and when it is issued, distill in the hot, sticky eye oil or a mixture of honey and water or fenugreek boiled with honey into it, then heal it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have similarities with the eyes in division, and that which is necessary for piercing; do according to health. You should make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from light due to the sun, and hold the oil clean and squeeze very hard; then place the paper of the oil on your left hand if the eye is on the left, or on your right hand if it is on the right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or take with your left hand if it is on the right; then place the instrument's point beneath the crown through the thickness of a nail in that area of the oil at the lower part of the smaller eyelid, then push the instrument called "almagda" skillfully, and hold your hand still until it pierces through the oil, and feel that almagda reaches the empty space; and the measurement of the way almagda should be at the full length of the measurement of the distance from the pupil to the end of the nose; and this is the crown of the oil; you will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the corneal tissue, and then place the instrument up to the location or the eye, and press it down along another path. If the eye bursts now, the patient will see in front of him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest and if the eye rises along the second path, press with the instrument, and when it is completely inserted and it does not rise anymore, turn almagda gently by moving your hand slightly; then put a little bit of gem-oil back in the eye, and squeeze the oil out from inside. Then place oiled cloth or dampened wool soaked in rose oil and abundant egg, and bind with the clean oil. We and those of our time put crushed comfrey with abundant egg on it.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard hairs, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", which is shaped like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce only the conjunction, and do not go too deep, but make one thin layer, then insert almagda as we have said; and in the completion of the work prepare a bed for the patient, who should sleep on his back in two layers; he must be free from all movements, and take light foods, and not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and tie him according to his position until three days; then untie him in the same dark room, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then re-tie him for seven more days; and it is not advisable that you do this during the healing or immediately after the incision, but it should be done when the wound heals quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	When an abscess opens, you should untie the oil before the seventh day, and direct those who soothe the abscess; and when it is soothed, you should then untie the sight and place a bandage of one linen cloth over it for any duration, and remain in that dark room. And then gradually leave the room, piece by piece, and convert to his case; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country, they make almagda piercings, which causes bleeding, but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, nor have I ever heard of it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of almagda forms, because those who do not know them see them; and they should be of arain properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of these should be of the same subtlety, and the rear in four angles sharp.
de la char sor le neis	On the skin near the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes there are various types of skin growths near the nose that resemble scorpions with many legs; and if there are such growths or a growth enlarged with a dark color, and a growth soft with light color. In this case, for those soft growths not enlarged, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, and pour onion juice onto these growths and pull them out; then hold that which you can grasp with the sharp, thin spatula until you know that the entire growth has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be held, you should cut it with very thin and light instruments until nothing is left; and if there are abscesses or wounds, use the remedy as appropriate; and if these are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them so that the pus is drained and all the growths are removed, then pour onion juice or vinegar onto the wound.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the bladder does not work and moisture enters up to the palace (which means it is healthy); and if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is pus in the bone above, so the instrument will not come; then you must insert a large linen thread into the bladder as far as possible, pull it out while smelling it until it comes through the bladder from inside the mouth; and children in school often do this, and it is easy for anyone who wants to do it; then hold one end of the thread with one hand, and the other end coming from the mouth with the other hand, and know each other while we are holding the thread; do this until you know that the thread has rotten the pus; then pull out the thread, squeeze the blood, moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the bladder as before; do this for four days or more, until the ointment has corroded everything that remains of the pus; and then put a plank cane in the bladder for some days until it is healed, and if there is a need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the bladder, as one distills oils and medicines from the bladder.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and lead it thus; and if you see (a tumor), make a closed cane, and let the instrument be filled with oil or any liquid to purify the bladder; and have one handle on the bladder to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	On the flesh near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	In the head of the nose often arises a disease called 'telul', which grows and becomes large, appearing noticeable to the eye; therefore it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and burn it completely with cautery or hot medicine; and if it is delayed in being cut until it has become large, beware if it is hard, of a dark color, poor sensation: do not touch it with iron as this is an abscess inflamed, for when one cuts it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft touching, not dark colored, you can cover it completely, but be careful that the patient does not feel fear, and treat the area with drying and constricting agents.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuation come in one of these cartilagines (joints), it benefits little, except for some men. Therefore, when this happens to anyone, check if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together with a stitch, heal it until it is healthy; and if the lips are already separated from one side and the other, you must cauterize all the parts around them until they bleed, then bring the two lips together with a stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood powder on it, and incense pulverized; and place some plaster of strong or another plaster binding on top of the powders, and leave it until it dries, then heal it with ointment until it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is that you bring together the solution: either with needles, as I have told you in the abdominal stitching; or with thread, as we said before.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips of an abscess
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	For men, within the lips there occurs an abscess hard, resembling grains of peas, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, cut above each tooth, take it with pincers and crush in every part; afterwards apply the leech (leive) juice after the incision of vitriol powder, until the blood is stopped; then apply the lard (aisil) to the wound until it heals.
de la char des gencives	From the jawbone
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a swelling arises on the jawbone, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with tongs and crush its root, letting the blood flow; then apply vitriol powder or other drying powders to the area; if the swelling returns after the incision, as often happens, then you should crush it again and cauterize; it will not return after being cauterized; these are the forms of tools for covering.
des sordens	The sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes sores are assembled at the root of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the teeth turn black and greenish and decay, as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth smell; you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and scrape the sores or the scabs that appear, until there is nothing left; and do the same with the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowish and other spots, as long as they are cleaned; and if you remove what is at the first sign, it is good; if not, repeat on the second day and the third, as long as you have finished everything; and know that the teeth require various types of instruments for scraping, according to what the work shows, because the one who scatters the teeth has different shapes than the one who scrapes between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary that when you treat the tooth of its pain, you delay pulling it out as long as possible, for this should not be done; for this is a very high substance up to where there is no excuse for shaving.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is forced to pull a tooth, you must be certain of the correct tooth. Many times the pain deceives the patient, thinking it is a good tooth and pulls out the bad one; yet the pain does not subside until the bad one is removed, as we have seen with many lords; and when you are sure about pulling the tooth, first scrape around the tooth thoroughly using a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then move it to your fingers or subtle pliers at the very tip of the root and gradually, until it is well loosened, firmly hold the pliers; and keep the patient's head in your lap so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After removing the tooth carefully to avoid breaking it, if it does not come out easily, take one of these tools and gently push it from each side, as you have done before. And if the tooth is perforated or split, fill it with gauze where the holes are; and pull it out delicately with pliers so that it does not break during extraction; and be very careful working around the gum to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part behind, which will cause the patient greater pain due to the root remaining, as well as returning to the patient by the malice of the root more painful than the first. Be careful that you do not act like ignorant lords, who sometimes break the chariot and fail to bring what we have mentioned; but often they bring about this great illness through the roots that remain or the chariot that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is removed, wash the area with wine or oil and vinegar; and if bleeding persists, which often occurs, use vitriol powder; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one silences the teeth first, should be long points and large handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be large enough so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of good iron, and be toothed for gripping.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains when pulling a tooth, then you should put cotton dipped in butter on it for 1 hour or 2, until the gum is softened, and then insert the tongs called "algefri", which look like tweezers; and they should be made inside just like a chisel and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tools, then you must expose the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is known as forceps, in this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	Be large and thick so it does not break, and if the root jumps out with them, that is good; if not, help with all the instruments, as the shapes come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you aid with this instrument having two arms, in this shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and of this tool that appears like large pincers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this tool should not be breakable, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other tools, which are not counted; and the wise master finds his own instrument by himself, according to what his work and the disease show, because there are such diseases where the ancient ones did not teach any instrument due to diversity in ailments; and if it breaks a cart or another bone where it should not, then it searches for the tools that are required, which I have told you, and assists with gestures, as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and firm to hold the bone, so that it does not slip, but can hold and remove; then restore the place of medicines suitable for this, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, and it is small, then apply all this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to natural shape and are misshapen, even in virginal women, you must know if the tooth is not born after the dent, and is not properly aligned, and cannot be treated or filed: then cut it off; and if it is erupting with the tooth, take this instrument which has the form of a small beak, sharp at the tip, made of iron;
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle of the chisel should be held often for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, file it with a small flat file as shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file used to make needles; and with the flat file grind the tooth little by little, so that it does not move too much while grinding; then flatten the end at any rasp, and if the tooth is very sharp and bites the tongue, you must grind away the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.
