Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	If the teeth are loose due to percussion or falling out and the patient cannot chew food without them chattering, and you have tried medicines to hold them in place but they do not work; then you must restrain them with a golden thread, because silver threads become greenish and rot, but gold threads never do; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to tighten the teeth, take the thread and double it between two healthy teeth, then put the tweezers between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more; as long as you see fit up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue covering until the part where you started, and hold your hand subtly and skillfully, so that they do not move at all; and let your knot be near the root of the tooth so that it does not escape. Then grip the loose teeth with tweezers and assemble them, and place them back in their original position, ensuring that they do not prick the tongue; then leave them thus tightened for as long as possible, and if they loosen or the thread breaks, tie another thread; if it remains and serves for a time, then it is the form of teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy and two loose teeth, according to what you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out and is replaced back in its place, freshly and as we have said; let no one interfere who is not skilled and patient, and sometimes the shape of an animal bone is made and placed where it is missing, and it is tied as we have said, and remains for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this ligament comes under the tongue, naturally or by accident due to injury; the treatments for this are as follows: open the patient's mouth, keep their head steady, lift the tongue; then cover the nerve-containing ligament with a wide bandage, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, if there is tightness or not; and if it's due to sudden injury, insert an uncine and widen the ligament; but make sure the cut is not too deep, as there is an artery beneath; after you have done this, apply a rose or cold compress to the area; then place a linen tent over the tongue; keep the patient warm every night, so that it doesn't heal; if bleeding occurs, apply vitriol powder; if the wound doesn't heal, cauterize it slowly with a cautery called lentiginout, which is good for this. Then cure it with other treatments until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of a faint color or black or hard, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it's declining to blenchor and there is moisture, then insert an uncine and make a small incision with a thin spatula from both sides; and if the wound doesn't heal at your treatment, apply vitriol powder until it stops bleeding, then return to your treatment until you remove all the pus; then apply a cold compress and let it heal with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	There come boils within the throat which are called "godath", and they are properly called the two almonds. When you cure them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the reason of blood flow; but let it ripen, and then you will cut it open, or it will burst by itself; and if it is of a pale color and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cover. But first check if the abscess has cooled down and been calmed. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head should be in your hands, and open his mouth and take hold of the sergeant between his hands, and press the tongue under the entire instrument, in this way it is formed; and whether it is made of silver or subtle brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Keep pressing the tongue on the entire instrument and you see the abscess. Then take the hook and stick it into the almond, and pull it up more than you can; and draw any cloth away with it, then cover it with the instrument, forming something that resembles a fist. However, the chief are curved and one end to the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or brass:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this tool present, use pliers of this shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	Then when you have caught one of the almonds, take the other according to the same manner, and after incising, gargarize the patient with hot sharp and thin instruments, and if there is evacuation of blood, then gargarize the patient again with hot sharp and thin instruments, or scorches of pomegranates cooked or myrtle branches, and similar things, until the wound is cauterized; then let it heal completely; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat instead of the two almonds, if these appear, cut them in the same way as the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, namely one of small size; and I had pressed closed all the throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the obstructed conduit, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died within one or two days. The abscess was so high up that it had been pushed into the throat through both openings of the neck. I quickly pierced it, then pulled out a large portion of pus; afterwards I closed the other opening of the neck, opened her mouth, and pressed her tongue; after piercing the abscess again, I cut off a part of it, and no more pus came out except a little blood; and thus the conduit of the throat was unblocked for the woman, and she began to drink water first, then wine, and did not stop cutting down on the abscess for long time; the abscess grew again and filled the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I deceived it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it did not grow anymore; and I left those parts, and let God do with them as He willed after me.
de l’uve	Of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the tear-duct (uvula) is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; if it is large and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscesses are subsiding, and it is subtle, you must cut it; if it is round and swollen but not long, it should be assembled; if it is red, bloody or black, you must make an incision in it. There is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it as I have said, according to its thickness and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, press their tongue on the instrument we mentioned earlier; then make an incision in the uvula, pull it out, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned for making the incision of the two almonds. It is not necessary to cut beyond the natural limit, because if you do, it causes pain and discomfort afterwards. After the incision, use what was said earlier about making the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it heals. If the patient is afraid of being cut, use an instrument for cauterization to overcome their fear. The method of cauterization is very painful. It is that the patient puts their head in your safe hands, and then you press their tongue on the instrument we mentioned earlier or in the chapter of cautery, and hold it with hot live coal, but not too thick or too bright; and use the handle of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has hair or some substance that you can put medicine on, such as the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument entirely over the medicine on the uvula; and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine but do not reach the throat or the pharynx; then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it against the uvula, for about half an hour until you see it redden and the bites of the medicine are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with all the cotton on top of the uvula, allowing the cotton to stick to the uvula; and repeat this process until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry for 4 or 5 days. If you need to start the cautery again using the medicine, do so, and after the cautery rinse around the uvula with cotton dipped in burr, clean what is around the medicine; wash with cold water and treat with gargarisms until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision, not just cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this way, take camomile, yarrow, origanum, rue, and wormwood, and put them all together or some of them in one pot, add ashes, and make it boil; the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and have one vessel with a cover inside the pot according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it should be made of silver or lead, and one of the eyes should be held shut by the patient until the steam rises into the eye through the channel, until the eye is putrefied; afterwards, it often needs to be repeated, until the eye dries out, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the abscess heat, because many things happen then; and do not do this for anything other than the decline of abscess heat. And if this is not present, take a channel and put an eggshell cracker inside the patient's head, so that their mouth does not get too hot; because the eggshell cracker does not let the steam burden the mouth, and it is good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often it sticks in the throat, bone or fish spine, or something else; therefore you should pull out what can be seen, and press the tongue against the sun until you see movement of the object; and if it does not open and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will expel the object. Or, the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cotton, or a radish root, or a small piece of dry bread; tie one thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; when it reaches the place, it will stick, and then you can pull it out. And if it does not come out as we have said, take a piece of wood according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and lift the head high; watch that you do not touch the epiglottis, so that nothing harms it or pushes the bone inward; it is better if the patient puts the instrument, because he can move it or the thing is easier to move; if he pushes it down, or pulls it out completely, keep the instrument equal until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	the vein of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes, the vein in the throat is treated with medicine as I have said in the division, but if this does not help, then look at the throat of the sick person in the sunlight, and when you press his tongue against the instrument that I told you about. If you see the vein, cut it with a small scissors or fine tweezers suitable for this purpose. And if this is not effective, take a curved needle, insert it into the throat of the sick person, then bend the tip of the needle one hot iron, and repeat this frequently. Dip the sick person in cold water all day, then take a full ounce of cold water in a glass, open the mouth, pour it in and make him drink, and move his hand frequently; and as soon as the vein feels the cold water, he will vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, you should fumigate the patient with asafetida, at the instrument I mentioned in the treatment of the eye; do this many times, for it will not cease easily. The method of fumigation is that you take a pot or one containing charcoal, and cover it with a perforated cloth, and the head of the instrument should be placed within it; then pour your fumigation, and the patient places the head of the cane in their mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape but comes up to the nose; and the smoke will now cause sneezing, and if it does not fall, continue the fumigation many times; let the patient suffer thirst, eat salty and alkaline foods, and drink no water; then it will be necessary for it to come out by this means.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument to treat the nose, is like scissors curved for entering the throat; and resembling the beak of a syringe, and it should have sharpness of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see below its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many things resembling abscesses are mentioned here, according to what comes later in this book from one and the other; they differ in perforation and incision, and it is in .ij. ways that one is similar to the other, and of these, which holds moisture. And the second way is about the places where they are on the body. Because abscesses of the head are different from those of the base, and abscesses of the charnut place (possibly a type of joint) are different from those that come in jointures, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if abscesses should not be perforated while the bowel is still immature according to its completion; and if there are such as it is necessary to perforate when they have become hard, but do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that come out of joints. Because when abscesses come out of joints, and they are left until they ripen around, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, causing contraction in that member. Or if the abscess is from the main part of the body, and perforation is delayed until it has matured, it will harm the main part; or if it is from the base, perforation should be done before it matures; and it is not advisable to perforate a hard abscess without digestion completion, except that one which is from the base, which can penetrate completely, and be lengthened inside, and a fistula forms; and it cannot heal in a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time for perforation of the abscess that is ripe according to completion, and it is when the pain is alleviated, and the subsiding of fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the opening and narrowing of the abscess's head, and other signs; and you should make the perforation where it depends more on the abscess, and where it has opened up; and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	1. When the limb is broken, this should be aligned accordingly. And when an abscess is in a hard place, it is better to leave the perforation until it is confirmed in digestion as we have said. For if you pierce before that, the body will fill with much pus and the wounds may become hardened and deeply infected. And for any abscess that are pierced according to the size of the body, depending on what the limb requires.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess has no head, like a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain part of it; stop up the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing wrong; do this several times gradually, until the pus comes out completely. This should be done very carefully, especially with weak patients, women, children or old men who are debilitated. The pus may sometimes jump out with the discharge of the pus, which could kill the patient, and you would not be to blame. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound, and see if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a large hole, bring linen or old cotton threads; and if it is a large abscess with many holes, it is necessary that you bring a thread in each hole so that they come against each other; and if you have pierced the skin of the abscess and shaved it around, it is necessary to fill it with old cotton or wool from flax without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then unbind, and cure it with ointment until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold water and linen cloth, moisten one linen cloth, and place it on the wound several times. If the bleeding persists, administer treatment and care, and the powders I mentioned in this book to the affected area, and if it is winter, or the wound or abscess is very nervous, you must put hot tents and moistened linen on it; and if it is summer, and the wound is fleshy, you must put moistened linen on hot oil, or cold water and oil, for up to three days as I have said; then open the abscess and drain it, and care for it until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to approach treatments for abscesses, and now here is the chapter.
des soros	on les doibt traiter par cautere de feu, et si c'est li soros qui est gros ou si c'est en estete, il faut les fistraire ou les aignorer avant; et s'il sont durs et ne puissent pas fistreier, alors les coupez en peus et empoignez le tueu par dessous la poix, et mettez feu au cautere, et on les brande comme il se peut, et ains qu'il soit bien chauffez, pesez le cautere et mettez l'en une vase d'eau, et le tirez hors du tueu qui est oste; et lors que li soros seront toutes ensemeies, si les clavetiez ains qu'il se refroidissent, si com il covient.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	1. For small abscesses that come on the head, there are methods known to us, similar to those in poultices, as with a plum-stone; there are some fat ones and others with moisture, like boils; and some hard and stony ones, without any doubt that the arteries do not work against it. And the operations of the neck should be tried on every instrument called "entromissoire", from which the following shape is derived, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, it must be done above the long way. And when the moisture is emptied, scrape without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, for it returns immediately when nothing is left; then immerse cotton in Egyptian ointment, if available; otherwise, in water and oil, and apply to the wound, leave until the next day; and those who remain will heal by themselves. And on the second day, repeat the cotton, as before, on the third day, until you know that it does not stay overnight; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed. And if the abscess contains one nut-sized fat, press according to this form, along the long way; and pour your eyes (or drop) on it, and scrape from all sides, and apply all your care to draw out pus where it lies; and if the arteries work against it, do as I have said before. And similarly with a stony abscess, and treat and cure as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the incision above a hard abscess and a moist one is lighter because they contain little blood. And if some of these abscesses or heads have no moisture, and from those I pressed an abscess on an old woman's head; I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had cut into it, it would have made as much wound as a stone. In other abscesses coming from heads, whether they be those that come on children's heads and the roots of the ears, they should be opened all days as long as possible to let pus out; and they should be treated as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Often this abscess occurs at the neck, under the armpits, and in hollows, and sometimes it appears elsewhere on the body, and they are swollen and infected one with another. Each scrofula is properly located within its own side, as we have said of the lump on the neck; and these scrofulas have many appearances. There are some that contain moisture, and there are some malignant ones that do not want to obey health. Therefore, when you see a good disposition in touch, and it resembles the color of the body, and is silent from all sides and not affected by the vein of the neck or the artery or conduit, and is not deep; then you should cut it open from above, and remove the skin from each side, and put two lips of the curette on the incision, if necessary, as we have said in abscesses of the neck; and pull gently and gently, and be sure not to cut the nerve or the vein, and do not use the spatula too aggressively or too deeply, so that your hand does not slip, and look not too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	If you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow you to finish, put vitriol powder into the wound, or some powders that stop blood, and hold the wound closed; let it stay until the abscess is calmed down, and let the wound soften and start to break up. And when the pus is drained, return to your work, as long as you complete it; then check whether there remain small scrofulas at the root of the main scrofula, if so, cut them and cleanse them. And if at the root of the scrofula there is a large vein, do not cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang out, without harm; then use old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and heal the wound.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you gather together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, as there is no need for excess due to the size of the scrofula. It is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, draw pus, and sew it as we have said. Scrofulas with excess growth, pierce where it has matured; and pierce it in the same way as the one mentioned earlier, depending on it, then introduce tweezers with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply an ointment of rejuvenating char, until it heals.
de squinance	If you make a bloodletting from the artery, then you must bind the veins that are near so that the bleeding does not continue, and close the wound with clean cloths.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the size of the throat, but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have quinsy, it is required that the throat slit called "epiglottis" should be opened; and no help should be given by these [affected areas], because all veins and the entrance of the sickness are in those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the tonsil, it is required to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it under four circles or one small slit through the middle, between the four circles or by the amount of the incision of the saw, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And if the neck is to be cut where the epiglottis is located, there should be no cartilage and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is afraid, then it must be that he stretches the skin of the throat all the way to the chin, then cuts through the cartilage until it reaches the trachea; and cut away the vessels of blood if you see anything, and then close the opening with suture as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the cutting of the trachea, which bursts through the broken neck and by the lack of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed in which doubt of strangulation exists, bring together the two lips of the wound and sew it closed with care, taking care to avoid the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Abu'l-Qasim says not to do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged dead, and the bird pecks out his eyes.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then you tie the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe through his nose and he breathes through the wound, and thus he is preserved from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And for this reason, the ancients commanded to keep the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it has passed in 3 days or 4.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	Then they ordered to sew up the wound and heal, until it is healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a girl take one dagger and thrust it into her throat, cutting part of the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was summoned to treat it, and found it just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound and discovered blood coming out of it, and that it had not opened or led the vein except through the throat, and the veins were flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I quickly sewed up the wound and cured it until it healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And there was no danger to the maiden except her voice became red, and she returned afterwards to her position.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	For this reason I say that in the treatment of the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia" and is a large abscess with a yellowish color, and it is common in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it is according to two ways: nature, and accidents; where the natural has no device.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And accidents are according to two ways, one of which is similar to fatness in us, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us by artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it should not be worked upon in haste but only in the small one, and it should be proven and examined with all the incision.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you prove it similarly to fat, and it does not swell at any vein, then strike it as we do the nose, and draw it out completely if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And carefully examine it completely, and treat it as necessary, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways of ours there are, which I will explain all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now I must tell you all the difference between a notch and a dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	A dislocation is characterized by heat and fever persisting until the inflammation has passed, and then the purulence is complete; afterwards, the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	A notch has no heat or fever or pain, and contains a blister, which is its own sac and is the same color as the body, and begins like a pimple, and becomes larger.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And there are two types: fat or moist, and they have the same colors as I mentioned in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the care of the sick, that you examine and test first all the instruments called "entromissoire," according to its shape or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiry for abscesses is that you take or more moist place that you find within the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you feel that the instrument has penetrated to the core, then according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then draw out the instrument, and be careful not to let it slip out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs out of the wound, make it have color as I said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	If no moisture comes out after the incision for the abscess, know that it is filled with fat, then make a cross-shaped cut on it, take hold of it with forceps, and peel it slightly from both sides and pull the covering or coat that you draw out healthy with it;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out healthy, pull it off in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	If there is nothing remaining, the nose repeatedly returns many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little remains and it does not trouble you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, hold the wound, apply hot things for easing the abscess, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the nose is large, make two lips on the wound, and treat it with remedies that cause growth of flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is swollen in contrast or other cases where you are forced to act quickly, use the leech of vitriol powdered, leave it for 2 or 4 days until the wound starts to heal, and let the evacuation of blood stop; then return to treating the part that was left with new dressing.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the first two sentences translated into English:
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are like the needles used for sewing silkworms, and they are of citron wood, iron, or silver, and yellow ones are more effective, and black-handled ones are more suitable for encircling the swellings of a fistule.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they come in three types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of tumors are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and some tumors have two bumps in four ways;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are tumors with four bumps in four ways; and there are tumors with two bumps in four ways as well as tumors with one bump only, and they are all necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The tip of these [tumors] where they are cut is sharp, and those that do not cut completely from one side are the ones we scrape the nails with, so as not to hit the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these instruments, the cauteries are held in loops, so that the patient does not harm themselves at the opening of abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	They are of four kinds: large, small, and medium, as you can see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And it is not used except in soft flesh, such as legs, arms, breasts, and in similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And sometimes another small instrument similar to a pair of scissors is used in this shape, with which blood is drawn:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is put to the place that stops bleeding from veins, arteries, and sometimes returns according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they resemble female breasts:
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain swollen and ugly, and whoever wants to treat them should do it according to this shape of the line B up to G:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then cut the fat, apply medicine on the wound with soothing herbs, then stitch together the two edges of the wound to heal it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the wound sinks downwards and is swollen due to its size, as it often happens with women, split it into two halves at the top, through two similar cuts;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	Thus one part is kept connected to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line encloses the smaller one according to this shape, from this line b up to line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then, remove the skin that is between the two lips, and take out the fat, and apply what has been said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary for treatment, until it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed, or the incision has not been completely made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it drains out the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes des asselles	From abscesses of buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the buttocks are cases of hard scrofula where there is moisture contained within them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire bowel in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat it with ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula (or scrofulous lesions), then make incisions in it as we have said before in scrofula incisions, and if the wound swells, apply a cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	The cutting of an artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut and the skin is sealed over it, there are often abscesses, and the same happens with an inflamed vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if it is known in this way whether it is for the artery, then the abscesses are long within.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when it is felt with your fingers, it indicates tightness; and if it is for the vein, then it appears wide open.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	It is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the shoulders and angles and near the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, the iron cure should be removed, and the one that is on the head should also be removed, and in the case of inflammation of an artery, they should make a long incision through the skin above it.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then open the abdomen as usual, and carefully separate the aorta from the intestines, while it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert a needle and pierce it through to the other side, and tie off the aorta with a double thread, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then prick the space between the two ligaments with a lancet until the abscess comes out, and let it drain.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply the cure that is called "beech bark," as long as the pain persists.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then heal the one with ointment following this, as long as he is healthy;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the size of the vein, then you must paint your hand with it that you can from the abscess to all the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle beneath the skin that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce through, and have one double thread so that you pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I told you, or bind one of the two sides with two strings.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you doubt that the thread did not enter, push another needle through all one thread beneath the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four leagues;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then press the abscess so that the excess is inside it, then press the excretion of pus and leave what is connected;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place on one damp cloth moistened with vinegar and oil, then provide it with treatments of tents and liniments until it heals;
des apostemes des ners	from abscesses of nerves

de la circoncision	Of circumcision
