De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In the amputation which is made all through the thread of iron I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the saw cuts exactly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, you saw equally all the time; but that the thread be well tightened around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you do not tie him to the rod except to tie the thread around it only, and then release him in all the ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then make it be between your hands straight, and place the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then push your hand to the mark and blow or say a spell, and draw it up until the head of the arrow is in; then clean it well of the filth that has gathered there, then tie the site with a double thread, then tie it under one peg to another link; hold it at two fingers by the second link, and break between the links, then quickly untie the knot and pull the head of the arrow out;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Let the blood stop little by little, for it is the poison; and put powder on it and on the powder one cloth glued with a soft egg yolk cooked without salt, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and let it be treated with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces for cleansing is as follows: the two heads should be tender and pierced, and they should be equal in size to the knuckles.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the amputation is when the cartilage within is cut; therefore, you must stretch it with your nail so that the joint becomes abscessed; and strike it evenly. And if you cannot hold it with your nail, take tongs, and then strike it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it exceeds three days, and that which is beneath the penis becomes swollen, let it be until the abscess subsides, and scrape lightly; then strike it as you can move it, and be careful not to damage the penis.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint with things that are submerged in a wound of powder, as we have said or treated powders, and if you strike it with excessive care, and it goes beyond [the limit], it will not harm; therefore, treat it as we have said until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	Retention of urine is from obstruction of stones, or frozen blood, or pus, or frozen matter, or similar things as we have said in the previous section;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not relieved, and you see that it is retention due to a stone in the bladder or the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over their knees; their feet should be placed on the back, and they should extend their abdomen from the upper part of the back, and hold the patient as tight as possible; then the neck of the bladder is compressed to force the stone out above, so that the urine is relieved.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, you must administer extraction with all the equipment called "syringe", of which this is its shape: It should be made of subtle silver thin hollow reed, like a bird's feather; and the tube should be a palm and a half long and delicate at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	The method for the discharge of urine is to take one double thread, tie its end to a piece of wool or cotton and insert the thread's tip into the syringe; then attach excess length of wool and push it up to the tip of the syringe, then oil or butter the syringe and an egg yolk, and make the patient sit on one seat, and you should rub the bladder and the penis with moist oil of olives and cold water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis upward toward the anus; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and let the patient feel it come up to the empty vessel, and this is not done according to the order for this reason, because the guide that leads it is twisted; then the thread is tied to all the wool pieces, and the urine follows the wool, then remove the wool, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And fill the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient is prepared.
des maladies de la vessie	On the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorches or blood comes in the bladder, or pus is assembled there and you see it distill liquids and medicines, then use all the instruments called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed with three holes: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see; and the spout at the top so that the medicine flows out well through the rod without addition, if possible to draw moisture, and push when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see that your medicines are thrown into the bladder, place the head of the goat in the moisture, and draw it through what is within; if you draw the moisture towards the goat's head, and then push strongly the drawing back; it will enter the goat's head, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the shape of the subtle enema with which one cleanses the bladder: it is as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or iron, and the head is higher; below it, there is a chain or cord; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture you want to enema the bladder with in it, then tie it between two cords using a good double thread, and heat one end of that moisture over fire; then insert the head of the enema into the penis, then hold your hand on the bladder with all the moisture coming towards it, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment and make one circle, and pierce it roundly around; then put a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle like one does with a thimble, and put inside it what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, press it with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the methods of stone and its extraction along with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone caused by the rain, and all the signs, and in which stone one should operate in size; and in the bladder, and in the vein; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder occurs more often with children, and this is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder, resembling urine in its subtlety; it opens the narrow passages, irritates the patient's organ, pricks it many times, and then binds it; and much of these leaps cause the foundation to weaken; and the healing of children is easy until they reach 4 years old, but it is very difficult in the elderly, and it is a moderate illness for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, first cleanse the patient with an enema to draw out all the feces that is in the intestines. For it sometimes hinders seeking for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, bend and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and protrudes slightly upwards. Then make him sit between your hands arranged below, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declining towards the bottom; then press and touch it with your fingers.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone within the cavity, hasten now to cut into the stone above it. And if it does not fall out with the touch of your whole hand, moisten your left thumbnail, if the patient is a child or an adult who is still weak; or use your finger, if the patient is a fully grown man; and push it into its foundation, and try to remove the stone. When you feel it at your fingertip, push it towards the bladder's neck; then press firmly and push it away in the direction where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch out his right hand upward and remove the skin that is under the testicles in the area where you make the cut; then insert the spatula spreading, which gives it its shape.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And place it between the area between the testicles and the foundation, not in the middle but to the left side of the scrotum; and it should be straight above the stone, and your fingers should be at its base or on its foundation, and the incision should be long horizontally, but narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance, the pressure must be applied to it (the affected area), which is the foundation, so that it jumps out without exerting too much effort; and know that there is a stone or an angle, and edges: it should be pulled out; and if there is one that is swollen, resembling a plum and round, from which the dislocation occurs lightly.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	Therefore, where there are edges and margins, make a larger incision; and if it does not jump out, then you must pull with pliers (tongs) that are shaped like a file at the tip to extract the stone without causing it to escape or break; or you may use a small curved instrument placed at the tip to push against it; and if you cannot manipulate it in this way, widen a little hole with a drill and remove it without cutting.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one stone, first push the largest one at the bladder's neck, then strike it, then pull it, and remove the smaller ones afterwards. If it is very large, it must be cut into pieces, making a larger wound. There are two possible outcomes for the patient: either they die or urine comes out immediately because the bladder cannot heal; but you should still try to extract or crush it using pliers until you pull it apart in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it closed, then place a damp cloth in oil and wine over it, or in oil and cold water and rosewater, to calm the abscess; afterwards reassure the patient on his neck, and do not undo the bindings until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you undo it (the bindings), immerse the wound well in oil and water, then apply the ointment "dyafinicon" and "basilicon" until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	If an abscess and corrosion come in the wound and congealing of blood forms in the bladder, and urine is retained, which is known to be done without effort with urine: then put your finger in the wound, and drain that blood, for if it remains, the bladder will rot and burst;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then clean the wound that is fresh, easy and dry, and assist in all ways you know, until it heals; and it is necessary that all the herbs you use to treat it, you bind them on his thighs, and apply the medicine on the affected area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	If the stone is small and it cannot be led out with a rod or pushed in, and urine cannot come out; then heal it as I say next, you should cut it many times, except that you excuse yourself from cutting because of this cure. I have already proven this so.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod in the shape as follows and sharpened at four angles, pointed on one thread:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft of the stone, so that it cannot return into the bladder; then push the awl gently into the shaft, until it reaches the stone; and turn the awl little by little into the stone, as much as you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come out, then press your hand on what is remaining of the stone inside the shaft. Soon it will be broken, and will fly out with the urine, and the patient will be cured.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie a thread around the stone and another one above, then push the shaft towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out and untie the lower thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and heal it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from women's stones (kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that a stone is in the womb of women, and if it ever occurs, it is a great distress for the cure, and it is forbidden for four reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman skilled enough to examine her, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	The third reason is that perhaps one cannot find a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth reason is that the stone of the woman is deeper than that of a man, for which it requires a more profound incision, causing great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you need to do this, then you must take a midwife who knows well, and even if one is difficult to find, do not give up on one chaste midwife; and present a wise bailiff in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do whatever you command regarding the incision of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And look very carefully to see if the woman is a virgin: then her husband must insert his finger or tip and search for the stone; and if he finds it, he should press it down under his finger, and advise her to push her pelvis with her left hand against the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If he finds it, she should move it gently from the bladder entrance towards the root of the thigh until it reaches the root, then press on the stone at the root of the thigh near the mons pubis, where it is moved, and feel the stone in that area. She should not move her finger above or below the stone and should cut it off at its first small part.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then push the root towards the loins if you feel the stone and keep pressing until the stone can come out, and know that there are many types of stones: small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and some have grains. Know their appearances to determine the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the wound bleeds excessively, apply vitriol powder to it and hold for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, until the arrow is expelled, and have tools that I told you in the extraction of the arrow for men to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If the wound is an artery that has been cut, place powder on it and hold with bandages and not repeat this action, and leave the arrowhead and do not extract it, for fear the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the wounds have closed, return to your work, until the arrow is expelled.
de hernie carnouse	Of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	An aquous hernia is nothing but a gathering of moisture or pus, which is beneath the bladder that contains the egg; and it is called "pus," and sometimes it is specifically in the egg's membrane itself, if one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the bladder between the pus we have mentioned; and this does not happen except without any reason.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the growth of this hernia is due to weakness that comes from the bladder, and the matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from striking the temples, and this moisture may have multiple colors: either it is a declining color to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or white and watery. This happens more often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, it is the abscesses reason, that is, long like the shape of an egg, and does not open the temples, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	If there is moisture in the tissue itself, it is the abscess reason with part of the egg, and because of this one thinks that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if moisture is between the hide of the testicles and the white sack, it can be felt well; therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, probe it thoroughly all over its extent, so that you may recognize its form as described earlier.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, judge what is inside based on the probe that comes afterwards.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we treat it with iron, the patient should be purified according to our power and the fullness of his body; then lay him on his back, on something slightly raised, and put a lot of cloths under him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	Then sit on his left side, and instruct the minister to sit on his right, and extend the arm at one of the two joints near the shoulder.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the spatula, strike the skin near the shoulder along its length until you reach the bone tip, and make your incision straight in dividing the skin as far as the white fat, and remove the thin layer of skin according to your power.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the white fat deeply with one broad hole and remove all the fluid, then put your fingers back in, and stretch the white fat upward; do not touch the skin of the shoulder but only the fat; strike the ribs carefully, if you don't strike it properly, the fluid will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the egg (meaning: fetus) jumps out of your work (procedure), reset it in its place when you have completed the operation using the forceps; then, stitch together the two levers of the keys (bones at the joint) with a suture, and then treat the wound as you would any other injury until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to bind the vessels that are suspended (attached) with caution, fearing the release of blood; afterwards, cut through the suspension and extract the egg, treating it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	If the wound is divided into two equal parts (meaning: there are two branches), know that this is two rami (branches); then cut through the other part as you have done with the first equally, drain the blood, and place damp linen soaked in rose oil into the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And put another dampened wool in vinegar and oil on top of the two cushions, and cover with double cloths, and bind it all together with the linen string according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths and use woolen padding according to this appearance and sew them together at the belt of the braces. The first head take on the foundation until the back, and the other at the part of the handle; and the second head on both sides, and the rest should be tightened in the buckle of the bracer.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this small ramic of fire is used as a medicine in the place of iron-cutting, and it is that you take one sharp cautery scalpel, and cut the skin of the cushions, and heat it as we have said, so that the white pus that contains the water is exposed;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If one takes the fire-cautery according to this form, and pierces it through until it is hollow, and peels off the skin with this subtle cautery heat:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And be careful in all ways until you reach the marrow; and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more healing; and beware of bleeding, and be cautious of the works of amputation.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if anything happens contrary to this, or abscess or bleeding or something else, then treat what happens contrary to this, according to what is mentioned before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work due to its horribleness, you should perform perforation as I tell you, and it is that when you are sure by the signs that we have said, piercing is necessary there.
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	Make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below the whole spatula-width wide, and make the perforation long along the body; and let the holes be large, so that all the pus flows out.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on top of it and bind it, and leave it to drain the remaining pus, then treat it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the white linen cloth does not allow the liquid to flow from the wound's mouth, you must insert a reed or instrument used for draining liquids from abscesses, as described previously; and enlarge one or two holes in the wound, and verify that the liquid returns, and it heals after 6 months or so, and when it is healed as before, the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess in the eyes
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	For in this section of the treatment, where there are many possible positions, it seems to me that moving is beneficial.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I will tell you the work and the similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Then many abscesses come from the body, and similarly from the joints; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is due to excess of bitter and acrid humors that spread to the joints, or from blows;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	The color of the abscess is similar to that of the body, and no pain is found, and it is a severe abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by chance there is an abscess that is hard and rough, of such color, and sometimes comes from an artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is due to an artery, it can be recognized by the hot position of the abscess when you press on it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you should not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	An abscess caused by swelling of a vein can be recognized by the appearance when pressed with fingers. et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	And can anyone well make an incision on this likeness, and on the others.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Then you cut the fat of the eyes, and the yolk above, and the white is separated from the membrane, and all the suspensorium of the eye is released from all sides of the eye.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already soft with these newborns, then you must draw out the egg, and cut it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is outside the white or in that which is inside the vessels, you must release all that softness and cut it round.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the hernia is at the rear end, you should cut it all out and extract the egg as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is done, apply the wound with moistened linen in rose oil and wine, then heal it with other treatments until it heals.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the kidneys
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enclosed in a covering resembling a small bag, with the softening of the kidneys,
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	And the patient speaks hoarsely when going.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the remedy for this disease is as precarious as the one before.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	However, we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	You must make the patient sit on a raised seat, then attach the suspension device for the lower abdomen to your chest,
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	To all the bladders which are near to the penis, stretch them out straight, and brand them, masters.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then pierce the swelling sharp wide across the bladders, until they are exposed.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then scrape from each side, as we said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then I insert an awl with a single thread of flax and tie it at the first place where the vein appears, and tie it directly to the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then grind (or pound) the shoulders straightly, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupt moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then heal the wound as one would another, so that no cowherd's stool should fall into one of its corners.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	because by this, no harm comes, and if all the cowherds come, it is necessary to draw the stools from them all.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their secretions due to the cowherd's stool, and they dry up and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the sifac
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The occurrence of this case is through the incision that comes or sifac, or extension on the abdomen in the area of the flanks, because the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is either due to sifac or extension of it, and these two methods of movement occur from various causes: either by percussion, jump, fall, lift of heavy load, or similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is of the extension of the dislocation, are that it happens little by little, in a long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the abscesses are even up to the full extent, because the intestines push the dislocation after it.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it is of the section of the dislocation, are that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear differently, under the skin near, and this is due to the outflow of the intestine and the body turning away from the dislocation.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines come out through the hernia, and are retained there, and cause great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments there is fear, therefore it is necessary to escape from them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	The method of the work is that you instruct the patient to insert their hand inside the intestine into the wound, if they can reach it.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then lay him on his back, between your hands, and lift his legs.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then place the intestines above, and cut all the skin of the scrotum along its length;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then insert fingers into the sides of the waist according to what is necessary for opening the wound, and so that the eyes can come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scrape the fat that lies beneath the skin of the cheeks, until the white fat is fully exposed on all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then insert your index finger into the following cheek, between the first white fat that lies beneath the skin of the eye, and the second white fat.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And remove the one that is behind the eye, and between the second white fat; then turn your right hand within the cheeks of the eyes, and raise the white fat to your left hand, and lift the eye towards the waist with all the white fat.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And command the minister to stretch out the arm upward, and dislocate the one that is nearer behind the elbow.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And command your fingers if there is any intestine entwined or white pus, and if you find anything of the sort, push it into the belly beneath.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and push it into the back part of the pus, which is behind the skin; after the waist, then cut the parts that appear to be from the threads, until there are four threads left.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	Then assemble one on top of the other in a cross shape, and tie it with the ligament below the hinge of the shoulder, with a strong cord of 2 parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then wind the threads of the tendons together, and tie them with a cord of 2 parts, so that no one of the vassals who feed it can enter within, unless abscesses do not come.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and make the knot straight along the first long cord of 2 fingers, and after these 2 cords leave the sinew which is below the hinge of the shoulder the great one of a finger's length;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and afterwards according to the roundness that the egg carries; then strike in the part which is beneath the skin of the joints, as much as it needs correction, and bend, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply dampened wool in oil, and put it on wounds, and there bring the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the whites are cauterized as we have said, after the incision, due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this often happens, and leave the ligament until it has chosen to slip [back into place]; and if it is slow to fall, then moisten with warm water, and put on what we have said, until it slips [back into place].
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound with other care, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a carnous hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I never saw anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like a branch which is together with the bone, in this manner that you tie the vessels, after the cutting slightly below.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then press it together and treat the abscess of those who work it, until the vessels bleed; and treat it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes comes rotting in the groin, as we have said, and open the vessels; and do not remove any intestines from the hernia, and if it is done, it is too much, and repair it every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And if it remains too long at this point, the wound or abscess swells so much that the internal contents are expelled;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	This happens through the extension of the abscess, which is inflamed and angry, as we have said, for it becomes swollen and opened;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the treatment is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	And it is that the patient lies prone on his back between your hands, then you strike the swelling of the wound enlarged according to the thickness of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	Then extract the pus that is beneath the skin which surrounds it, then take the iron and place it on the apparent part of the swelling;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	Press firmly on the stomach, then place the two apparent parts of the swelling on the head of the iron and press both;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then remove the iron head, and do not strike or extend the swelling, nor anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of the anus.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then heal it with wound treatment. And when you bandage the wounds, if they become infected and the wound is healed, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The fistula (li sifac) is closed, and it has no appearance in the wound, and the cauterization is performed in this place, and it is closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin around the eyes
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin around the eyes becomes soft in some men, because the charms that are inside are softened and it is visible; and when one wants to heal it, it is necessary for the patient to lie on their back, and you bandage the softened skin on top of the natural skin; then bring together the two lips to a stitch, and if you see, sew first the excess skin that is softened with four or five stitches firmly; then bandage between the stitches, and heal as other wounds, until it is healed, and stitch the thread.
dou chastrement	The punishment or correction (of a patient)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	In our law, the punishment or correction (of animals) is mentioned, and I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the animals respond when questioned about their ailments and cures; the other, because we often need to punish certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and pigs and others. I say then that punishment or correction is done in two ways: by attraction or by cutting. In the one that we do by attraction, we seat the animal in warm water until the skin is softened; then we grab it with our hand, holding it until it is reset and you no longer feel it. The punishment of cutting (castration): you should dye the animal and press the skin around the testicles with your left hand; then tie the suspended instrument, and strike above each one as many times as you have well cut off the scrotum; leave a small amount of fat and the subtle fat that is on the vessels; this method of punishment or correction is more effective than the one done by attraction because in the case of attraction there may remain some part of the testicles, which causes the animal to desire lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites (intersex individuals)
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodyte is according to .ij. forms in humans: one such form is between two openings, as the figure of nature for a female, who has hair and sometimes urinates from it. And the other form is in women, who have something above the penis like a rod and two openings. The treatment of the male and the female is that you cut all the adjacent parts, and treat them like other wounds; in the second form, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the openings, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	The translation for this line is:
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is an adjacent part on a natural part, when it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as one hand, and that is its treatment. You should dye the excess of the tentigene with your hands or onions, and lightly cut it; do not go too deep, so that no bleeding occurs, then cure it with another treatment until it heals. At another place where a boil emerges from the mouth of the vagina, and it bursts out, resembling a cow, hence it is called by the ancients "cow disease." You should cut it as described for the tentigene, and cure it until it heals.
de erratique	From erratic [or wandering]
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	When the nature of the woman is not recognized or the birth passage is narrow; and it is natural by birth or accidental due to illness that has come upon it; or it is from falsehood, subtle or thick, and it occurs fully formed in the marriage bed or in the costumes or underclothes, or elsewhere; and they should be prevented from conceiving, and giving birth, and accidentally producing flowers; and recognizing these things is through the observation of the midwife. If the discharge appears soon at your fingers or at the rectum. If it is subtle and near the two leathers, hurry up, and press them in this way: put your two fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two leathers, as long as the subtle falsehood is firm, and hold the discharge; then take wool, wet it in oil, and place it over the area, and let the woman lie down flat each day, so that it does not heal. And if the falsehood is hard and thick, you should cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. If the discharge is from a false childbirth, suspend it at the navel and cut; and have the medicines for stopping blood, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together with a lot of egg; then bring a wide plank for a diaphragm, so that the wound does not heal; and in this way let it be prolonged, and bring a tent of dry linen; then cure other wounds until it heals. And when there is false childbirth in the marriage bed, it should be covered according to this method, unless it is an abscess swollen. For one should not touch an abscess that has swollen in the marriage bed.
des emorroides	Hemorrhoids [or Piles]
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Emorroidal openings are openings of veins which, without cautery treatment, often become swollen; and when emorroidal openings grow old, they turn into thrombosis; and as I have said in the division, we have described their resemblances, their signs, and I will here describe those that receive treatment. I say that emorroids and thrombosis, when they are completely within the anus, and cannot be felt by touch, cannot be treated with iron. Those that are at the entrance of the anus can be felt, and these are the ones that can be treated. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold room, then take hold of the thrombus with tweezers, grasp it by its roots, then sprinkle medicines restricting blood, such as acacia bark and dragon's blood and incense and similar things on it; then press her feet to the ground for an hour, then immerse them in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and grape seed extract and gall nuts and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make one poultice on her back. If it stops bleeding, that's good. If not, apply fomentations to the back and breasts without cutting; then take linen cloth, wet it in the juice of plantain or elderberry with old wine, and apply the fomentation to the place. And when the abscess heals, treat the wound with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a small hard lump, which should be covered as I have said for the thrombus; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	emorroidal openings (of the anus)
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many forms of abscess appear in the anus, such as boils, abscesses with pus, herpes, fistulas, emorroids and abscesses that burn, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division. It is therefore necessary to describe in this treatise the abscess that burns which appears in the anus, which is not one of those that are covered with scabs; and if you want to know how to work with iron, check whether the abscess is aggravated at the beginning of its development, and filled with heat and fever, and turning red if you can see it. Then do not rush to pierce it, but let it heal until the pain subsides; and then make the patient sit on one seat, or two small seats where he leans, and support his back and his feet at the parts away from the leg; and spread his thighs, and place his arms beneath his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then suck out the pus towards the right side of the body, and bring in the tool used to open the anus, as follows: and it is necessary that when you bring this tool into use, that you first pierce the tip so as to know the depth of the anus, so that the tool does not enter too deeply as it should, and does not burn the patient. If the tool is larger, then cover the depth of the anus with cloths, so that the tool does not cause pain; and place the cornet of the tool on top, and tie the tool. And when the abscess opens, and it becomes soft in the hand, then cover it with a linen bandage; and when the boil is empty, then put in the hollow of the wound tents moistened in rose oil, or green dry oil; and place the tent far from the anus and above the tool linen that has been washed in water or cooked malves are; then cover it with ointment after two days, until it heals; and sometimes lift the anus and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then of water or long roots of lys Aristologe that have been cooked. Then return to the ointment. And if the wound is reopened in the anus, then you should be careful not to use iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	From childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is first necessary for the midwife to recognize the figure of natural childbirth and its signs; when you see the woman contracting below, desiring to urinate; then hasten to help the child be born; then know that this birth is according to nature, and it comes out headfirst, followed by the afterbirth; and when you see these signs, you should lightly press her abdomen so that the child is born quickly; for when it descends onto its head, it follows with it, and the husband removes its waste products in good cleansing. And that which comes out otherwise does not come naturally. Sometimes it comes from the feet or the body or the thighs, or it may turn around accidentally on the neck, or by other bad positions; therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skilled in these matters, and to avoid errors and deception, and I will show you all the figures as to how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out headfirst by natural birth and the woman delivers with effort, and her vitality is weak, make her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; then anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then insert the midwife's little spatula, as shown in the following figure:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And cut the second (placenta), and strike its nail (umbilical cord) until the moisture that is within it comes out; and hold the woman's belly as the infant descends, and if it does not descend, you must cleanse the woman with mustard seed of fenugreek oil; then make her take and vomit emetics, and keep her mouth and nose shut for an hour: this will now cause the infant to be born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	about the delivery of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the infant comes on its feet, you must push it upwards.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	And then turn it bit by bit, until it is even.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then take one piece and stretch it bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can he jump up to the knees, if he commands to take hold of it, and make it vomit from the inside.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If God wants him to fly (if possible).
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it little by little until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Therefore it should be done gently.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come as we have said, take mastic from high altitude, oil of sesame, and melted resin, and grind everything in one mortar.
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put this ointment on the female nature within and outside of it,   \]   Car c'est la mieulx que toz autres chose qui sont apres le mesure.   \]
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	Then make him sit in deep agony underneath the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it is softened below, make one collar of myrrh, put it underneath, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then make him sit on a chair, then make him vomit and hold his mouth and nose closed, and press the belly gently, because the infant is jumping now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the birth of the child on its genitals
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the infant comes in this shape, put the bale on it hand by hand.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then lay it on its neck, with the legs hanging downward, and lying on one bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	fold its hands hand by hand, then take hold of the hands above, and uncover the buttocks underneath until it is prepared below;  \]   et si il est en mal gre, si li pendent aval de la croupe en sa cuisse droite, et li preint ses testes. Et si c’est une feme, si i le fet les poignetz, et il oste les cussins desoz si com li fist en male;   \]  and if it is in bad condition, let it hang down from the rump on the right thigh, and take hold of its head.
