et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And you should sever the cartilage that is between the two joints to one space of a thumb's breadth wide, while the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then you sew or silk, and place on each side one linen cloth so that the silk does not touch the healthy bone;
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another physician comes to treat a different wound or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And when blood flow occurs as you work, cauterize the area immediately.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	and you put on some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then bind the limb with a firm bandage and heal it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man in particular:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	It happened to him a blackness resembling a burn by fire.
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	And that corrosion started first in his thigh bone until it consumed the entire thigh;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corruption, he covered the thigh with a copper sheet, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	And long time afterwards, the corruption or tooth of the hand came back to him, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I placed things repressive after the purification of his body, but the corruption could not be stopped.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	Then you command me to amputate his hand, but I do not wish to unless I have hope of curing the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	And he doubts that if I am to amputate his hand, he will not die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the power of man was weak; and he lost all hope and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and struck his hand with a sword, and recovered;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have considered this only for the purpose of doing otherwise, if it is needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess appears in a charnut place and remains so long that it forms a large swelling of boils;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then they run and burst, and the skin is left open like a wound, as if a vassal were wounded;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	The skin that is above is as delicate as linen fabric unraveled.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	And it will not go down to the bone or nerve, and such disease is called "sain".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it becomes so long that it goes to the bone completely, it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And the cook [surgeon] should know that you should wrap it all over, and in the same way when it is subtle, as a bandage.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And it shall not rot for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the leather will rot, and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if the leather is thick with flesh, then cure it with clysterism in this way:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Check if the breasts are large, and if they are swollen with a foul smell.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then use the Egyptian clay poultice which is made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take asafetida, oil, and litharge equally, cook them in one vessel over fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	And then take from these [substances] according to your need, and make it into vinegar and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and clisterize the breast, and compress the wound;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	leave the medicine for two hours, then remove it by pulling gently;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this repeatedly until the breast is purified and pus removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	And sometimes it is caulked with watery ash,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you must take vine ash, pour water over it.
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then strain it and use as a clyster, until you know that the breasts are properly healed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor watery ash.
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	If the poultice is made with water and honey or has a little bit of pulverized litharge;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you poultice it with honey and sweetened wine, the honey should have properties of cleansing and washing.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the vinegar strengthens the blood.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this and trust that the breasts are well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	If the cluster of this (body part) that produces pus in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and apply a plaster to define its boundaries, and make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you plaster it with certain medicines and ointments, as I have said the properties for treating wounds.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the wound in the breast is small and the plaster cannot enter it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	If a small wound from a blade is made, put an Egyptian bandage on it.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and apply the ointment of basilicon, while it is still wide.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, make an incision of one league or apply a curette.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if a swelling that arises above is present, press or squeeze it lower than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bone is in place, do not let it be encumbered with cartilage.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast beneath as you see,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	prepare in such a manner that the bone aligns with its lowest point.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the boil is fully formed, do not allow anything to be inserted into it.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the wound beneath as you see fit,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	if it appears in this way: that the boil runs slightly downward, and do not allow anything from the boil to remain.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	take medicines that are consolidating to put on the wound.
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	And they lay a linen cloth over the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then apply the force on the wound in the breast, about a finger wider than the first one,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then anoint it with oil according to the size of the wound,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the breast wound to bind it, and do not remove the larger cloth except after several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And one who is on the peritus of the breastbone, often has the breastbone taken out to remove the swelling,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and knows what to do about the swelling of the breastbone, whether it is poison or pus, or if it is digested or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and takes care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been spread out in this manner and you see the nature that rises on the peritus of the breastbone,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	If you know that breasts have swollen, approach them with care;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then unbind it in the morning or the third day, and when you unbind the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	change one or another bandage and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	If the breasts overflow with undigested matter for many days, know that the breasts do not swell.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisonous worms crawl after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for the healing draws near. For there are men whose wounds delay in healing and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the belly swells suddenly after many days, know that the breasts do not loosen.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast delays in growing, and is swollen, apply drying medications with a moist substance and dry properties.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	As an ointment defined, for it contains much vitriol, and it is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take the ointment defined, and make it with rose oil, and mix equal parts of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook and use it; and the same made, warmed and swollen,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when the defined ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	Take myrrh, aloe, and incense, grind them, and sprinkle the powder on honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then place one cloth on it and lay it on the breast, and sometimes an astrologer gives a long one,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and root of the celestial lily, which is as fine as flour and centorium.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simple or compound medications: grind them, make powder, put on the honey I said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the wound is long, and it is not treated by this method,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption sets in fully, and it presses into the bone, or hardens the members or ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of the fistula is by the method we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the nail bed
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panaric is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the hand.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or under the toe, or by chance may arise in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes inflamed, and no care is taken, if one abscess bursts out.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And they run and throw the bowl until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance they may strike the entire thing.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And the corruption reaches the bone, as long as it brings a foul smell, and the shoulder is wide at its base, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment does not help at all.
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	If this doesn't work, then you should cut off everything that has remained of the nail.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is very beneficial if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses against the flesh after it, and begins to swell, and becomes blistered,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	you must place the rod under the nail so as not to touch the flesh.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	And lift up the bone, and strike the cartilage gently and lightly.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And put on top of the remaining cartilage medicinal burning and corrosive substances to burn everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	If the corrosion is in the bone, strike and pull it out because as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the bone broken, strike it with a hammer as before said.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wounded, and bruised, and feels great pain, you must heal it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then strike the nail with the sharp instrument in cutting across from above.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	And be careful that the incision does not reach the flesh below the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If it happens, put something on top to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the hand gradually subsides.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The fingers that sprout from some men's hands by accident are all fleshly.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	And by chance, it has nail or bone, sometimes it has a claw,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Sometimes they grow at the root of the joint, or the growth is in some fingers of the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	A nail that grows under the nail of the finger does not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And he who is born at the joint of the thumb, by chance becomes mute;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of the one who is fat is light, in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	the length from its root in a broad spatula;
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure, take care.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In a newborn or an unborn child, you must first cut the round cartilage to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together in the fingers also come together by birth, or by injury, or by fire burn, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cut the joint, so that it repairs according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two tents or dampened cloths anointed with rose oil, so that they do not stick.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	and you place between two thin planks, until the edges are joined as required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Similarly, if it comes to either of its sides with the palm, you strike the joint as necessary.
Des vils	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large, enveloped, and filled with melancholic superfluities, which come in many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	It also happens in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things more than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purge of bile at times, and then the healthy from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron cure is according to two methods: one is by beating them, and drawing out black blood through it;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And another way is to open a vein and pull it out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is done in this manner: make an incision in the leg with sharp hot water, until the flesh becomes softened.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then hold the patient's leg from above the knee to below the knee part.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then cut open the vein, either one or two or three, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then draw out and drain the black blood from the vein between one end and the other until as much blood as the sickness can bear comes out.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it up, and instruct him to bind himself with black-colored meat or linens.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and begin the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and help the sick person.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The swelling of it is as follows: raise the leg of the patient if there is much hair on it,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then immerse it in water and rub the leg with warm, hot water until it turns red and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have water, heat it on the fire, then press it against the vein along the thigh or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then scrape the skin with an edge of a knife, and remove the vein from both sides until it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And one sees it red and black, and when it enters or skin seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the rod beneath, until it has risen in the skin, and then pierce it lightly along the edge.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then strike it into another place below by three fingers; then scrape the skin over the vein as far as it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift the rod, as you have done, and pierce it at another place, as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then take another size [of instrument], or more if needed, then heat it up, and place it on the base of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Heat it again and re-heat if needed until the second size; then take it out gradually by size, until it has come completely out, then place it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, push an awl with a single, strong and double thread through it.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and pull it out and draw it, and push a rod underneath it, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And keep it from bursting, for if it bursts, one cannot draw or lift it out, and this harms the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it all, place on the wound linen moistened with vinegar and oil of rose, and let it heal until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vision is twisted, contracted and rolled together in one, not straight as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that you cut it badly (the dislocation), but do not cover it; draw it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to pierce the vein is curved and does not cut, do not pierce the vein with it.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of large curvature, for if it is thin, it will pierce the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is opened in the legs, in warm places where no grass or trees grow, and in dry ground where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and it may happen elsewhere than the legs, and this is due to rot that comes from beneath the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	if snakes come within the body and go out, open a vein between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	If the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a very large swelling in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then change the joints, and start to open the vein like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head opens, it is necessary that you wind around a piece of wood from 6 to 24 inches and tie it,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the wood on the leg, and every time it slips off, wind around the wood again and tie.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it and wind the remaining around, but do not cover it at its root until it is all out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	If you pierce it (the shoulder), it goes back into the flesh, and brings forth abscess and pus or evil disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this reason, it is necessary that it be treated bit by bit until the head, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes, this vein is when it is treated for five or ten fingers of length,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	And once a man came to me, from whom it issued out ten fingers' length, and when you cut it off, press half a pound or more, and pierce it to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out of it; and empty the matter that is within, and bring medicine poultice to the place for three days, then treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	Sometimes this vein swells up again, and especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or hand.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And it comes much from falls, and what causes it to rain; cure it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often affects cattle,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	And there is a small worm which is born between skin and flesh, and it travels through the whole body swelling and shrinking,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	It feels itchy around each member from one end to the other, as long as the skin where it is located swells or it moves and jumps.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	It is infested with putrefaction of certain fluids, like worms, snakes, lizards, or roundworms in the abdomen.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubt is had about its mischief, for when it goes through the body, it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	By chance, oil enters and is destroyed; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it to cure and drain, one can only force it when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	Then you must lie the limb above and below with a strong rope tightly,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	Then beat above and pull harder, and if the wound is completely healed and you do not feel it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If you cauterize with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greater harm that it does is when it burns oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold a cork beneath it in the shape of a circle, then strike above, and pull it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and you must use the patient with body cleansing of soluble medicines for removing bad humors,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it swells with meat pork putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called on our land "vakirir", and is pain that comes in certain members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And then moves from member to member; I have seen this as I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and within a short while, it (the swelling) rose towards the shoulder as if like a worm.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	quicker than anything else, just like living silver when cut from one piece.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain separates from that place and pierces the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	Then a little later, it runs through the entire body until it comes to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then told me that it turns again around the body, as I saw it do.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from one member to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Therefore, I would have wished that many had wished to move pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I did not wish it, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this, such constrictions appear;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not appear accordingly to this reason for those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and veins responding.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	When you see treating this illness, and the patient feels such pain as we have said, if it opens as we have described,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	press down firmly on the joint above and below, then apply pressure above until the swelling is compressed at its site.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	And cauterize the joint; if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not cure those that displace the wind (windbag or intestinal blockage), as with fetid pills and pills of serapion, and similar others.
Des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their shapes and according to the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of theirs is such that there are those who have large points, small, round, and solid.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some have two angles, and of those who have tongues, and of those with parts.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and when it falls in any member, it falls in two ways: either in the main body which is hairy,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or spleen, liver, heart, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls (the limb) into any position of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you later appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you should take care in the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many positions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if this sign does not appear to you at all, and the arrow is not embedded fully, draw it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the skull when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and if there is a bulge on the forehead above the skull:
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It is concerning cataract, stone, and gravel in the eyes, redness of the eye, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps without fever from the nose or ears; and perhaps losing speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumping from the wound with white moisture resembling pus, and also bleeding like a bruise of flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, hold on to the treatment, and draw out the arrow if it isn't in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of an arrow when it strikes or pierces is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were embedded in a hard object, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And occasionally the arrow becomes like hair and produces black blood in the court, brings coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore one can sense doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that never pierces the flesh is when bubbles rise from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, sighs loudly and seeks fresh air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if an arrow falls into the mattress of the bed, it is removed between the ribs; and it causes great pain, deep breathing, and groaning; and all the limbs of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If an arrow falls into the stomach, possibly something from indigested meat may escape from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If an arrow falls into the belly and nothing escapes from the intestines through the wound, there is no hope in the treatment or removal of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, as the hand, arm, throat, shoulder, armpit, backbone, waist, hips, legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of this you do otherwise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man that an arrow or spear struck him in the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried and pulled it from the other side beneath the fat of the ear, and it was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And pulled with force an arrow that stuck in the oil (fat) beneath the paper (skin) below,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was found, and not a bit of it could be pulled out towards the front.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, with its tip very sharp, piercing the ears without any harm or adverse event happening to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And it pierced an arrow from the throat of a Christian and the arrow was Arabic with sharp ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was a barber and became skilled in pulling it out, and the Christian remained unharmed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And pulled an arrow out of a man who was either head or belly-wounded, and thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And after he has passed thirty days, his dislocation does not change position;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut through the arrow, manipulated it, and pulled it out without any bad incident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if one wishes to pierce a man with an arrow who has been sewn up, and the wound is closed;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And the arrow remained inside [the body], and did not change its position naturally.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor did it find any hindrance in any of its natural movements.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And a second man, who had an arrow strike him in his face, and the wound was sutured;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained like that enduring great pain; and many similar things happened.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And through a (arrow) shaft of a man, one of the princes king, who was wounded in the neck,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly tilting towards the right side; and the arrow was completely straightened
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it after it had been wounded for three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I seek it with great subtlety, and I feel it not.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he feels prickling and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of the arrowhead
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I place it on the loin attractant digestive, because the loins do not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And the tip of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the plaster for many days and healed the wound directly, and the patient remained for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	He felt the arrow within his body for a day; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I apply corrosive medicine to the wound by hand for several days, until it is healed.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and press, and feel the head of the arrow which adheres to the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjust in the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appears clearly visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and after passing well the terms of four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And then cut open the wound that I have lanced, hold it apart from both sides, and it cannot be closed.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I continued to refine and devise various ways of tools, until I took them for a day with well-made tweezers.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I treat it and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	Then I will restore it, and the wound will heal, and the patient will be completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	I have told you about the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	since I do not say everything, for the books cannot cover everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	However, wise masters compare very little concerning this matter, and regarding what is present and failing.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	True are nine works, and nine tools, in the diminishment of things strange which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not enter the limbs where they are inserted except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the side where they enter, or from another direction.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And this one that jumps out through there or enters, is an arrow entering into flesh, and jumps out occasionally.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out, leave it until the flesh heals around it, and make sure the wound is closed.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days and move it daily.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps [the joint], and if it does not jump, pierce around with all [a small sharp instrument] until the joint is loosened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow has been driven into the skull bone and goes up to one of the brain ventricles,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And some of the accidents I have mentioned to the patient: do not draw it out immediately, but let it heal evenly after several days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow comes up to the shaft, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is inserted only into the bone but does not come up to the shaft, and
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	The patient remains for some days without any serious incident, if the surgeon extracts it carefully.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply inserted and cannot be removed, administer poultices around it, as I told you before; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if an arrow is inserted into the body so that it cannot be seen, seek it out with all your might;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, draw it out with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow make it difficult to remove:
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein in the way, open the wound as wide as possible.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	And pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on the arrow as it is,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	and remove the foreign body which is inserted into the muscles by two parts as much as you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	then break or fold the ears of the arrow, as much as you can draw it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	Be very careful to not break the arrow, pull it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot pull it out in one go, push the linen cloth around it until it is reached the joints, then pull it gently, as the extraction should be done carefully.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	If the flow of blood opposes you, bring to hand what we have said in the chapter for its treatment.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of incising nerves and veins, and use tools as you can pull the arrow out safely.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	In haste or immediately, firmly or gently; place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, or it opens something of it, or the skin is swollen near it as can be seen or felt.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Therefore cut through it, as far as the tongs can grasp, and then pull it out: if it leaps away now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, let it stay for a while, then continue with the extraction until it issues forth.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it were of the arrow shaft, push it all the way out.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it fell out, and you wish to administer a binding, then apply one bandage.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	If the point of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; then push forcefully,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is embedded in the hair, apply the instrument point for easier extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow has touched bone, then it is necessary to cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then care for the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls or pierces through the belly, bladder, side or kidney and is close by, and you can cover it over, then do so;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and guard against covering the vein and the nerve, then extract, and sew up the wound if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	heal it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used to extract arrows resemble an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape at the arrowhead is also like the feather of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to point the arrowhead, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pointing and straightening is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	incisions of the body common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Incisions for venesection are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen heads
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	it means: two basins which are behind the ears, called "herbech" (herbech in Old French is not translatable as it doesn't have a direct English equivalent)
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two temples visible (temple is the area on each side of the head where the skull is not covered by skin)
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins which are in each of the two eyes, called "aspirates";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is at the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two tendons which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on top of the lips above the mouth, and these are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	2 veins located beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly drained are 5 in each arm.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is called the cephalic and is found on the left side, commonly referred to as "vein of the head" by laymen.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the median is called the "fast vein," composed of both the cephalic and the basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the lay people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And the lay people call it "vein of the stomach", and it is above the abdomen.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	That is the one which opens up clearly above the navel.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salivary vein is the vein between the auriculare and annular, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and foot are three veins: one of which is beneath the hollow of the left thigh.
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle of the right side, and the vein called "nesses", which is in the ankle on the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The veins after the ears aid the ancient catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of the healer, as I tell you, and it is that you grasp the patient's head,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the vein or vessels are with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	If you have pain in your thumb and feel its pulse beneath it, squeeze it.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance, and push it through under the vein up to the bone, then pull your hand all along the vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut the skin and the vein well through two thumb-widths deep, and make the blood come out as much as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then tie it and let it heal.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The sanitation of the two arteries that are in the temples, is effective against migraines.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and sodium, and eye strain, and to the heart of watery eyes for the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of sanitation are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is necessary for the patient to stretch his neck, until both veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse beneath your thumb, then press firmly;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the knife tip on the vein at the top of your index finger, and thrust the needle underneath it;
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	lift up the vein and cut it, just like you have done in the two other veins, and take out the correct amount of blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then bind the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then form the bandage, and leave it until it heals; and we have spoken of its covering and its removal, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the healing of the skull in old facial diseases, and it has migrated and turned red.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the qualities are such that the patient stretches his neck while twisting it, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", of which shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	Place the point onto the vein and strike with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the amount that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient's neck and tie the vein until it is sealed and never use a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Moreover, the flames should not be too sharp; and pierce through obliquely because the bone is close, and accidents may occur if the flames are too fine.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The veins of the two arms aid the eyes, and the ligament, the tendon, the muscle in the oil, and the diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of its veins is that the patient pulls their neck in a twist using some cord, as previously stated.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then, the vein or veins should be heated with a stick of fire about half long and wide, as there is no need for heat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the fire is subtle, perhaps it breaks; then make an incision for the blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with a cloth, and secure it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The purification of the vein from the navel is useful against ague (fever), and against pustular scurvy (a skin disease), and against diseases caused by bile.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	just as migraines and redness that comes from the liver, especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the purification is such that the patient grasps his neck, then grasps his navel with your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the subtle flame long, and push it between the two nostrils.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the vein does not open well as it should, and the arteries will now begin to bleed.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too deep, and make the correction of blood according to your need, then let it rest for a night, for it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The salves of the two kinds aid in the extraction of the gallstone, and at the beginning of an incision, and in many diseases, and in stopping itching, and in corroding, and in sores, and in ulcers.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the qualities of the urine are such that the patient strains his neck under both, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And the master stands over the head of the patient, and the patient lies on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then open the vein along its length a little wide, then draw the blood moderately, as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then, you must reset another place in the other vein, then unloose the ligament, and hold the veins gently,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Do not let the patient strain it; leave it until morning so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	On the Healing of Livestock
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The translation of the given line is as follows: "The opening of veins in the lips above helps in cooling in the mouth, and in corruption of the gums, and cuts in the lips, and toothache and around."
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the vein are to make the patient sit before you, and hold their neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and they are known by the fact that they are dark, and the fact that small veins surround them;
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Take both of them then, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Take the largest of each pair, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below; because it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the saliva beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The saliva from the veins beneath the tongue helps after the cephalic vein puncture, and it is used for the treatment of throat diseases and mouth diseases;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the qualities of the healer are such that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts the tongue, and gazes into every vein on both sides.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then, let one and the other (veins), not go too deep, for beneath them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins near the surface, which are commonly healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or burn with large mirrtin flames, or subtle olive oil as you know expensive tranches, and it is called "anesil". (Translation)
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and thin according to the width and thickness of the veins. (Translation)
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of mirrtin flames is very renowned, and it is wide as you see: (Translation)
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it must be used to open the veins that contain large and turbulent blood. (Translation)
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And this is the form of olive oil fire:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more pointedly subtle, and is for refining subtle veins with citrus-colored thin blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The refining of the basilica (which is one of these veins) helps with diseases that are under the throat, neck, chest, and stomach.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	It is necessary for the Lord to refine it properly, and he should evacuate the artery that is beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if it touches the artery, and bleeding occurs, it should be stopped, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be pressed by the fire, but cut as an anise seed.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the bladder does not open openly, you should open it and change another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or if you want to take any urine from it, or if the vein opens in its place on the arm: it opens openly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the cope (cup) to fire annul, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	If you wish to know the location of the bone, then you must also stretch out the arm and touch the place where you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the location of the opening, then tie the arm, and cauter the vein with fire.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And be careful not to hit the artery when you see it swell, for it is of the artery; cut it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if it swells high like a child's urine, and the surrounding area is red and tender, know that this is not of the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Therefore, hasten then and place your finger on it for a long time, then cut your finger so that the surrounding area stops bleeding, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Keep the arm still, and let it be in this position, the patient should not move it; be afraid, and do not move it until it heals.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the wound is not stopped and it bleeds, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is open, as the head of the artery retracts; stop the bleeding in the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of fustic bark, cut it and take one half and lay it on top until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it (the wound) stops bleeding, that's good; if not, heal it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of bleeding should not be hurried in many positions due to the small size of the wound and the power of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The bleeding from the vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above and from the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and the cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And it is necessary for the master to pierce through the nerve that is below, and if it perforates too deeply, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and inflate and heal the wound may grow sick again, and by chance it cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens frequently, and if it does not open in any men due to its subtlety, then you must pierce it with the instrument anesthetic; and cut the nerve as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healing of the skull helps when it draws blood from the head, and assists with the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to heal by pricking with olive oil or myrtle fire, for it is the safest of all veins, as there is no nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Furthermore, it is necessary to seek out the easier joint, and not to hurt anything when it must be done for the first time, and then we repeat.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And sometimes the joints swell in some men, when it must be done for the first time, but do not hurt anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound, according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about wounding is that wounding is not done except for the sake of health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future diseases.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the wounding should be done in one of the four veins that are known as follows: cephalic, femoral, or basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And it should be bled at the beginning of Lent and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And it should be bled every first or third day, after 2 or 3 hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding given for diseases has no fixed hour, but when it is necessary on day or night, at all hours and in every moment.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And one should not bleed children under the age of 14 nor women who are pregnant except for the first four months after conception.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	They should not heal the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wants to heal, in whatever way that may be, it is necessary that the intestines are cleared with a mild cleansing enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there is much feces retained, so that the veins do not bring excess waste from the intestines to the main limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	They should not heal who are too salty with meats, or drunk, until they have purged themselves, or water-logged.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if there is wounding after a colic attack, vomiting, abdominal distention, multiplication of women's disease, labor, watchfulness and fasting, and whatever weakens the power, or by weapon or body injury;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then purify the humors, if they are thick, with foods and drinks and medicines, if you have that power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then immerse or bathe it, if nothing prevents it, to purify the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	And heal the vein with the instrument at the side of the third [vein], as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	Keep him that day from work, from pain, and from lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And be gentle and kind, and let the healer be higher than him who is to be healed, and rub the arm twice or thrice.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then draw out the thread slowly, for if it is too tight or narrow, it cannot heal without.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the place with hands until the veins swell, and feel for them.
