puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then wet the hot iron tip of a thumb with a little old oil, then place your left hand's knuckle on that vein under the dislocated joint where you want to cauterize.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not break and fail when struck by the iron.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins like cords to the needle, and others that are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	When applying fire, it draws to the fire and cannot open the vein; this is with some of them.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	If it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, for this reason the surgeons should be advised on these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that's good; if not, continue a little below or above that spot, unless it is inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is inflamed and the patient is afraid, let him rest for one or two days and do not tie the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance, abscesses may come; do not enter the water, then renew the healing if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small or without a thin layer of cort (cortex), and you doubt that it will not bleed as much as you see, place the fire directly into the same opening.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and open it a little hurriedly, so that the flesh is swollen; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the flesh swollen, do not renew the healing, but put a little of oil on it, for the grease reduces the amount of blood in that place, and the oil is absorbed by the wound.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer oil of lard in each wound that you open a vein, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	Also apply treacle and bowwood to it when placed upon the place; divide it if it becomes too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	If an abscess occurs (which often happens when the opening of the vein is small),
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you are in a hurry, place a damp, soft sponge in warm oil and water on the location for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary that you do this after the blood evacuation from the vein, and if it remains in its place for several days without blackness or greenness, it does not matter.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, put something from aloes or myrrh steeped in wine or vinegar, mustard, or a similar substance on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And there are often abscesses and signs in the sanctuary of the temple: put your hand on it then, if you find it soft to the pressure of your hand, it is an evil sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not place anything of what we have said on it, for by chance in court without the artery; but make one dry compress to harden it, then heal it with another remedy until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each person according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it become thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is filled and hollowed out, and requires extraction of blood, to make a larger wound, and let the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to drain a little bit and often, and it must be drained by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of draining is safe from corruption of blood and nerve compression, and it works better than the long drainage rather than wide one.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body needs to be purged, it is necessary to give soft bread soaked in juices of pomegranates; if he is scorched, draw blood three or four times or.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexion, eat soft bread in syrup made from muscat grapes or honey with aromatic spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and anise, and a fragrant syrup before purging.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he is suffering from diarrhea during purging, after the discharge of blood, it is necessary that he drink a broth made from meat and a fragrant subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And apply other things as we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If one wants to fracture his arm, and heal it again at another time, if it is weakened by repeated healing, then let him heal little by little, according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to fracture his arm after the first healing, and has a strong body, let him heal in 6 hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to heal from another part, should heal on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because there is much blood within the body that has been heated up and causes fever; in such a case, it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and to enlarge the opening until it can be held with a hand.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you wash all the conditions of health, and place your hand on top of the feet when it heals, so that death does not come in its place.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	And this often happens, when the healer is negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not advisable when you wish to dislocate the arm, and let blood flow a second time, and the wound has closed, that you press firmly.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is curved, extend the arm as much as possible, for it would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it until it bleeds the second time; or you press it with the tip of the flame until the frozen wound opens.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put a piece of clean linen soaked in vinegar on top and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, leave it and do not squeeze it until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to draw blood a second time, draw it from the same place, or another vein, or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are opened at the location of the neck because they are composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of opening is that the patient plunges his hand into hot water until the flesh becomes red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then tie it gently, so that the vein appears well, then prick it carefully, not wide or long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make the incisions wide, and prick near the joint of the hand, and if it does not bleed out, put the hand in hot water and let the blood come out into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is summer, do not immerse the hand in hot water, for it should be kept longer in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the vein of this artery is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the caudate lobe of the liver is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it works:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Press the hand and apply hot water until the vein swells if it can be seen.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	If the vein crosses, and if you press it completely on all sides, it will not hurt anything;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not go too deep, for the nerves are beneath all uncovered by flesh.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then put your hand in hot water, if it does not freeze in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as necessary, put oil and wax on the wound to heal quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purgative of the hand on the left side is beneficial for the disease of mice, and do as I have told you regarding the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The poultice of the shin is beneficial for all diseases that are beneath the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	as for the diseases of the stomach, retention of flowers, diseases of the limbs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its poultice is that the patient should immerse their foot in hot water and rub it on the affected area until it perishes.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And lay [something] above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot it goes in many directions.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Take then the larger vessel, or at the ankle, for that will suffice.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	If you should raise [the vessel] above the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below, and pierce it similarly as in cutting; let the flames not burn it.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the limb cannot come out, put it in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	If the lesion needs to be made for the first time, then start again a little above because the place is salted.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same for the other limb equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the knee of fire, and its lesion is worth the pain of the hinge when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of his health are such that the patient immerses himself in water up to the knee joint, and then turns the leg four times above the ankle.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise, the vein will not open; and if it opens, you must heal in all ways that you can, and by crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	It is better to cut it off, for the limb is dead and very responsive to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not pull it out, there will be no healing for the joint that is closed or open at the foot or in the little finger, and guard against nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	Make such a correction to the blood as you see, and then untie the bandage, put cotton on it and press; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Wounds of the blisters
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blisters are made of horns, or hair, or glass; and blistering is done in two ways: either by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cauterization, which is meant to wound, is of two kinds: either it is for all fire, or with fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and this cauterization which is made by wounding and extraction of blood is performed in 14 parts of the body.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	because one part is entirely in the head, and the others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two others in the two sides of the neck; and the tonsils beneath the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the tonsils under the armpits; and the tonsils on the knees;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the tonsils between the two arms; and the tonsils between the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the tonsils of the wrists; and the ventosation does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And because of this, one should not hesitate at all, just like when performing venesection.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered in any case, nor to any fire or hot fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, due to necessity or habit, it is required to administer venesection, we will do so either at the beginning of the month or at the end, and in the middle and in every instance.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they have to perform venesection, have a swollen head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if such [persons] find swelling and redness in their face, head, neck, and darkness in the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such [persons] who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue is swollen and they spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if such [persons] faint, see blood in their urine and vomit blood, die, or similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially if it is outside of the month, we command to ventose after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sore in the mouth helps with the inflammation of the head ... which comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventosation is in place of the sore in the head,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it is not appropriate for one of cold constitution to use [the treatment], or who has catarrh, for it does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason, it is not appropriate that the elderly should use [the treatment], nor those with cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal themselves often become careless and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the danger of negligence.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The cupping glass in the neck is located at the place of healing for the head and basilica, and for this reason it is beneficial for the treatment of the disease.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to cut through the channel of the sphincter, and also to prick, and to fill up;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	it is necessary to press it gently, for if it holds too tightly, it can cause obstruction in the intestines or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	Wind in the two ribs of the neck is worth the pain of the head, and obstruction and migration, and strangling, and pain in the roots of the teeth,
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and is located in the cavity of the basilica; it is necessary that you command the lord to extend his hand to put it, so he does not touch the artery, and there is no loss of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventosations below the chin are useful for mouth disease and decay of the gums, as well as similar diseases found in the mouth; it is located near the salivary glands of the two lower lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosations of the shoulders are useful for disease caused by heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventosations of the sides are as useful as four veins in the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the master not to pierce too deeply, for the joint is naked of flesh and knows beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The blister that is on the buttock is effective against hemorrhoids from their foundation and diseases beneath, and it should be large and made of goose feathers, which requires good drawing; and if it were too fine, it would break; causing large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The blisters on the legs open widely because they draw blood from the entire body, and they are effective against ancient pains of rheumatism, marasmus, and the bladder, and remove inflammation; they are located in the joints of the knees and ankles, and weaken the body after long use, causing paralysis in many positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting on the cupping glass is as follows: first make it empty and fill it quickly, then place it immediately, move it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the skin turn red and swell, and appear the color of blood; then let it rest, and replace the cupping glasses, and take care in the arrangement of the body, for there are some who have thin skin and clear veins: it is necessary to make a single cut, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and one deep puncture; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If the skin is thick, then it is necessary to make two cuts: the first time to refine the vein's path for thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If the skin is very thick, then it is necessary to make a third cut; and when we want to draw blood drop by drop, we should only poke it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want much blood, we should often encourage it; and if the wound is closed, we should force it open fully, and let the cures be such that the veins are pierced suddenly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and who have closed pores, that you anoint the joints of the blisters with stimulating and soluble oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this case, with violet oil or sweet almond oil, or seed oil of cucumber:
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in fever, oil of cress, or of lilies, or of chamomile, or another similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amoradine oil, or balm of Gilead oil, or anise oil, and others similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if one wishes to heal a thin and narrow flesh with small pores, no oil should be applied.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it should be washed after the ventosation with cold water, or rosewater, or cold water of raspberries, or of cucumber, or of pearl water, or another similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise from asses' milk, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large surplus should rise from old wine, or water of sour milk, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not advisable to bleed before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after venesection,
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is necessary that he purge, when he needs to evacuate and when he is already evacuated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard the patient who is jaundiced and without is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	It is necessary that he take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And eat little meat, and cooked cheese, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And the one with a cold constitution, if he takes syrup of honey and fragrant mild wine (which is between old and new), and eats little, and eats soft cheese and small birds and young birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day that he vomits, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give some men sometimes tricolor or musk oil before vomiting, or afterwards, to strengthen the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let the wine be refined, but it is not suitable for those who drink hot liquids.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The boils that are placed on wounds are those that are placed on the liver, spleen, gout, stomach, kidney and groin, because these members do not bear wounding at all.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is done to draw blood from one member to another.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we do on the testicles when they are swollen; to remove the thick fluid from the member, as we place boils on the stomach and groin to reduce it.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And alleviate the pain when there is an obstruction or arrow, by chance it attracts the obstruction with its power, or causes the arrow to depart from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and so it acts when placed upon the liver and spleen when there is retained windiness.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these windy conditions are administered empty for sucking only; sometimes they are administered along with fire, and sometimes filled with cold liquid.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in diseases of the lungs, and in such a way this bellows is filled with hot water or water in which certain herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the bladder administered to fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And have it be .2 inches wide and half a palm long, and have it have one small hole on each side, as for inserting an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and be made of linen, soft in front so that it does not irritate the patient when placed on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And take in hand a rod of iron or steel, to set a plaster on it.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they should be large or small according to the diseases and age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the boils of children are different from those of old people, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And this bladder (or suction cup) should be placed on the member in such a way:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Apply this bladder (or suction cup) made of wax or linen thread to the middle (or base) of the vein that is within the vein,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the bladder (or suction cup) so as not to burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be above the wound as we have said, so that when one looks at it, if steam comes out, remove the bladder.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	Take the thread and wrap it as before, and repeat frequently, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the bladder that is administered for pleurisy, there should be neither a needle nor wound, and it should not be brought unless when it is full of water, and it should only be placed on the limb;
et c’est li forme:	And this is the form: [No translation needed for "et c'est li forme" as it is a French sentence structure equivalent to "and this is its form" or "and here is the shape" in English, without any specific meaning in this context]
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sooteries are not applied except to members where it is impossible to put leeches due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the bare parts of the body, such as hands or feet, and other similar areas;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the quality of the user is that when you find sooteries in sweet clean waters for purification, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put them [something] in warm water, soft, until they [the things] become familiar [soft], and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	Then clean them with wine and vinegar, then rub the limb until it turns red, and apply the salves.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are swollen and hot, if it is a place where vinegar can be applied, do so, for it is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the limb above a pillow, then apply cold water, and afterwards compress it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the joint becomes too swollen after the body, soak a linen cloth in cold water and place it on [the affected area], until the swelling subsides;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the wound is multiplying, place broken glass or similar things on it until it heals.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Place half-peeled beans on the joint and leave them until they harden to the joint, it will heal now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more snares, take others as well.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the snares do not want to be taken, rub the bloodless place, or you pierce it with a needle until the snares come out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they stick to it.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see them urinating, sprinkle some powder of aloe and crushed seeds or ashes on it, they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear child, that the foolish man abandons this chapter, for he will never see any of the ancient books, nor read a letter in it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason, medical knowledge is lost in our land, for I never found anyone good at it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I do not know anything about it, except through the knowledge of ancient books that I have studied extensively and treated the science, and through experiment, and the practice of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described it in this chapter what is contained, and I have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought forth, just as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary for us to say the prologue of this book the summary of speech and chapters where wise men put their understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who have experience know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you quickly bandage the patient on both sides, unless anything prevents you, such as weakness of the body, or children, or old people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the time is not very warm, or too cold; and eat cold food, namely cold meats, and meat of the eye and shin, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about abscess heat, or spreading of matter in the limb; then the patient returns to their first care as they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with foods that make thick broths, or they have thickness, such as cooked wheat in water, and meat of the head, and feet, and pancreas of cow, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	In prolonged nursing, the wounds break more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of old and weak people cannot be well healed or joined according to their nature due to the weakness of the members, nor those who are too tender, like the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no remedy, reset the broken bone (large splints) that straightens and joins the limb together, as much as possible like before; and do not touch it at all during this time, and for this reason, it should be fed with large foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are different in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the neck is different than the break of the arm or leg; I will tell you all the ways of a break in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that heal by growing together like the quill of a pen when writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if the break has an open wound, and the break is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each time has its device, and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory comes to its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	The fracture of the bone is known by this, that the limb twists and opens wide due to displacement, and presses on the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and if it has no twisting or touching, and the patient feels no great pain, there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it can have tortuosity, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand at all, but place medicines that come after here, and then hold it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks that go into the joints, and are the two parts dislocated, they must now be set evenly, so that abscesses grow there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if an abscess comes close, leave it for a while until the abscess is calmed down;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then equal it to the muscle that you can easily and skillfully move, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration of one with broken parts; then hold it, as required hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is hands or feet, or if with your hand it is small members, or if there are two ropes or one rope and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are dislocated, you remove all additions in their joints to the muscles that you can reach, and ensure that through your work there is no injury or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	Adjust well the two shoulder bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	Feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that they are not well aligned: straighten them beautifully and do not strain too much, nor force like those who make abscesses burn and contract the member by their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is set, punish the patient so that he does not move it, neither in watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not broken, and it should be put in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it straight so that twisting does not occur when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken member are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members vary in smallness and in size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and fingers etc.: it is necessary to wrap them in soft and thin linen bandages.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those which are large, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bands encompass the whole large member and equally constrain all parts so that there is no injury.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie light bandages around it, three or four times according to the member, and hold your hand a little on the bandage, then go above the fracture and tighten less than the fracture, then move away from the fracture.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the ligament little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another ligament, and turn it around reversely over the broken bone.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part below the fracture, and press moderately, not too strongly nor too gently, as we have said in the first lesson above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the ligaments of linen or cloth, until they are all even, then tie everything together with one bandage, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, put on it something soothing for the abscess and one who removes the swelling, and leave it thus for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then hold onto your arms (or legs), and they should be tied with a half-thickness of a strong cord, or a plaster rod, or palm branches, and shaped thus:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but the arm (or leg) that one places over the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And let it be as long as necessary for the member, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it in place on the pegs just as you did at the first joint, then bind it with thread coming forth, as you did at the first joint for the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	It is narrower afterwards, tighter; and it must be that the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their bonds with twisted linen cords, and that is great error; for the bond cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it must not have less than twice the space between each peg.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient has been struck by the heads of arrows in their joints after they have been set straight in healthy ones, place linen or cotton poultices over them so that they do not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bones are broken, I shall tell the cure below after that.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to set all fractured limbs at once on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when limbs are large, it is not necessary to set arrows before 5 or 7 days, or more according to your confidence in the abscess healing process.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the manner of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: it is that you take flour that is kept near the mill walls, and mix it with abundant egg, and put this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner for restoring the fracture in various positions, and especially for women and small children, for it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to make the plaster that restores fractures and dislocations and twists: Take barley flour, salt, linseed oil, resin of pine, myrrh, aloeswood, and mastic, .x. pounds; of balm of Gilead and aloe, .v. pounds; and make powder from these ingredients, mix them with abundant egg, if the constitution of the patient is hot, use this plaster, for it has a good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to make the plaster for twisting: take mastic and white poppy seeds, .x. pounds; myrrh and aloeswood, .viii. pounds; acacia leaves, vi. pounds; Armenian bole, .x. pounds, grind well, and mix with vinegar or abundant egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of plaster for joints and dislocated bones, soothing the pain that arises, and using it to shape the bone and break it: take new linen, moisten it with vinegar and cooked oil, and apply it to the area. This plaster does not restore [the bone], but it is good for soothing an abscess heat, and properly treating pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster to set broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth-parsley leaves, grind them together and make a plaster from it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of broken bones and for promoting the healing of abscesses: take root of wormwood, chamomile, violet flowers, bean flour, from each one a portion; grind them together and combine with wine, and if the members are scalded, use it with coriander moist water or plain water.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of poultice stronger than the first, when abscess hard comes to the restoration of the member. Take roots of comfrey, linseed, balm of Gilead, trefoil, and wormwood, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; grind, and cook with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates wrote in his book that no other substance should be placed on a broken member for restoration except for an ointment made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems Galen says that dry and somewhat warm things should be placed on a broken member for restoration, such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that is beneficial for injury and pain: take ground-up mugath and chevyl d'omes coppez (or pennes of oiseaux), and vismalve, and mix them evenly, and grind into a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then remove a small portion of it after that, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not remove it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching comes to the place, or there is no rest or swelling, hasten and remove the plaster immediately; take a light cloth and sea sponge moistened, immerse in water, and apply to the place until the itching stops and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then put dry linen on it, dampen it in vinegar or rose oil, and tie it with a nut until you are sure of the abscess heating.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member rest, and the pain disappear, then resume the bandage gently, add a little plaster, do not strain it too much as before; and be subtle until it heals.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess has healed and turned red, swollen, hot, and sore, and you need plaster and linen, apply it as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if no swelling comes to the limb from what we have said, do not dislocate it unless after 3, 4, 5 or 7 days; and sometimes leave it 20 days, as one sees, until the break heals, and the swelling approaches the flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then hold it more tightly than before, and let the flesh swell, as I have said before; but if you see the joint drying out more than necessary, know that no nourishment can come to it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then apply warm, hot water to the dislocated joint, every three hours, and slightly stretch the ligament.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Therefore, prick the nerves in the limb sharply and correct anything that foolish people do, which twists the limb: this is harmful, and such work is fearful; I see nothing else but to weaken it and work properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of breaks are, and various shapes, and the causes are intended.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are breakages made by sword blows, and the shaft breaks all the bone up to the shaft which is beneath the bone, as in a hack or thrust; and for this reason, this type of breakage is called "hackure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	For the sword strikes the bone from above to pierce it, and this type of breakage is called "absolute"; and the wound from these two breaks, whether large or small, is called "fracture".
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a percussion buried, or a cleft or shaft of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent fracture that approaches the membrane beneath the bone, or it is on the bone itself, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is healed to the bone as subtle as a hair and the fracture is small, it is called this type of fracture "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by striking with stone or falling, or in similar ways, causing the bone fragment to enter beneath, and the wounds are closed as a potter makes on the pottery; if an arrow enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones, like a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and these kinds of fractures are dislocated in various ways, as small bones are; and I shall speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the traction on them, and the exploration with probing, and by corruption of the flesh that is above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairy appearance is known to those who, when they have uncovered the bone and rub it vigorously, make the fracture blacken.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, beware of the patient's condition, and if you see any unfavorable circumstances, such as vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, paleness, high fever, hairs appearing and turning red, and other signs in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no unfavorable circumstances and hope for a recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the navroz comes first to you, and it is in winter, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the start of menstruation.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is not corrupted, and come the complications as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone fracture reaches to the tissue that covers the brain, it is necessary that you make an incision in the broken part: and it is that you take hold of the head of the patient, and expose on top of the bone in all ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound as soft as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if pus or abscess discharges bone, or abscess covered, help him as needed, and it is that you fill the place with dampened cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the abscess subsides and the flow of blood ceases; then proceed around the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways of working: one way is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is to have various incisions, some narrow and some wide, pointed and made with a sharp instrument, and work lightly to prevent cutting the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is dislocated and hard, then you must perforate it around (the dislocation), so that you administer splints with wedges, but not so much as to pierce through the bone of the chest; and above the point it should have a margin or a circle that does not allow the point to pass through the bone; and you must have more than one, so that each one comes in its place along the thickness of the bone, so that you have wedges for all sides; and this is the form of the four kinds of wedges:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for perforating around the broken bone are that you place one wedge on the bone, and turn your hand until you know that the bone has been pierced; then move the wedge another little bit, and do so all around, then cut the space of the bone that is between the fracture, and do it as subtly and lightly as possible, and gently, as we have said, until you draw out the bone or any tool that you have such as pliers or tweezers; and make sure not to touch the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have the bone pierced and treated, then it is necessary that you reset the fracture with any tool similar to a chisel, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other chisels:
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if some small bones or no scales remain, gently remove them with instruments; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work is the one that Galen speaks of, which is more secure, and he highly praises it, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must cut open a part of the bone where the fracture is visible, so that when you have exposed this part, you will place under it the head of the curved incision, which has the shape shown below.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut through from one side, and the parts are sharp in two edges, so that the cutting is toward the bone; then hit with a small hammer above, so that you lightly strike the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is beneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is swollen against the bone, then gently break the bone, because one can badly break the bone and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone does not break through to the cloth, and the bone is chipped only from above, and there are small pieces, then you must do this after roughing it up, and remove the scales with a sharp razor of various sizes, in order to make available the most suitable one for each place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	The patient should shave off large areas of hair, then proceed to finer razoring, and continue this process until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In the other haircutting and subtle breakages, you must bring appropriate tools according to his guidance; this is not a task that can be answered by one who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is exposed, you must take one linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, moisten it in rose oil, and put it over the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another cloth doubled over once or twice, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; do this more gently than you can so as not to irritate the wound, then apply one more bandage, but do not pull it tight more than necessary to cover the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And leave it for a day or two, until the abscesses have subsided, then release it, and administer medications such as lily roots, flour of peas, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and from these things make powder, and sprinkle it on the wound, and immediately administer unfailing medications without bitterness.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	Ensure that the wound is always clean, do not leave any ointment or bandages there, for when bandages are placed on top of the brain fabric, it will rot and become corrupt, causing great harm to the patient; for when sharp things are placed on top, it will burn through from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be careful to avoid any bad accidents happening to the patient as we have said, for it is doubtful and full of doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come forcefully except by medicine that we have placed there, of such virtue, then you must take a part of honey and 3 parts of rose oil and one piece of linen cloth, and lay it on the sore.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you must treat it in ways of wound healing, until it heals completely.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	It is known that sometimes the two parts of the neck above are broken, or one alone, because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilage, and does not break, unless it protrudes or twists, but heals again.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should place your little finger or thumb near the nose, and insert the fracture into the indicated index finger's pocket, and toward the thumb, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and perform this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the fracture is in the part above the nose and the thumb cannot reach the place, you should place it equal to the top of a small rod.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, you shall do likewise (i.e., also apply the same treatment), and hasten to restore it within the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed down, then bind a cloth of linen to the head of the wound where the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind another one from the other side, if there is a fracture there; and let the cloths be as thick as they fill the wounds of the head.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.
