And they said any restorer that the tents should be moistened with butter, and to grind each day. I do not think it is good, but they should be moistened in a mixture of egg yolk and milled powder; then leave the tendon until the bone is hard, and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one inserts goose feathers instead of tendons and wraps it with one piece of linen cloth and holds the breakage together, and blows warm air into it; then do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If an abscess occurs while you are working on it, put either cotton soaked in rose oil or a small piece of camphor on it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess does not come up, apply a plaster outside, made of flour of wheat and powder of incense, mixed with egg yolk, then put light poultices on top, but do not tie it too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	If the break in the neck is small and it is broken into small pieces, take out with suitable tools, then stitch the wound, and treat it with healing substances such as plasters and ointments appropriate for that condition.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no wound inside the neck, treat it with tenting (traction), and place bandages of linen until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	If the jawbone is fractured without any external wound and the break is not split in two but only displaced, and if it's recognized easily that it's just displaced, not broken completely inside, as can be seen from the curve.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side of the jawbone, put your index finger in the patient's mouth; if the break is on the left jawbone, use your right hand index finger and push the break gently from the outside, then align it with the other hand from inside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced in two places, you should provide extension to both places equally.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move or break, hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a splint of broken jaw, and place one double cloth; and place on the cloth a large well-made peg or a piece of equal skin, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it where you can, and command the patient to rest, and nourish light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the fracture changes, dislocate it on the third day, and then reset to its original position; apply a poultice with flour from a mill mixed with egg or meal of some herbs after removing the splint; place a light linen cloth over the poultice, and if the poultices swell and the patient's dislocation does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it will heal within four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess arises, apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, be careful not to remove any piece of the bone; if necessary, use subtle instruments for the extraction.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, expand it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is no more left, then close the wound, if it is wide, and apply one dressing suitable for this purpose to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the bandage
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks in multiple ways, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is of three types: either it is broken and dislocated in two places and divided into pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operations are when the fracture is accompanied by an injury, that you have two assistants, one to hold the shoulder where the force is broken; and the other to extend the neck towards the affected area; then make the dislocation equal with your hands so that the form is as it should be, without any appearance or misalignment.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, place a round cushion of cloth or linen under the patient's shoulder, and make it as large as necessary; then pull the limb and hold the cushion so that you can align the fracture as needed.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder outward due to its being deep-set, as it comes in deeply, then the patient must lie on his affected side, and place one ear against the shoulder, and push the shoulder downward, until the bone of the socket is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your hands, and if you find debris, then you must cut it upwards; pull the pieces gently apart, and if the bone cannot join due to any hindrance, strike one of the incisions that you have made; but place this instrument under the socket to prevent dislocation.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and resemble a ladle, not pointed, and be of such a size as required, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two handles, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as is the shape of the wound that you made when you treated the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of an abscess hot, if it breaks, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt the hot abscess, then use a cloth and bandages, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if pustules become hot, soak a cloth in rose oil, asafoetida, and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The bone compression, when it feels painful and swollen, is that you place the plaster of flour mill and egg white powder on top of the bone and put light packs on top, and put a spear under the bandage if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large bandage of one palm's width, then place a double cloth dampened on top of it and wrap it around; then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the edge of the bandage is hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the stick on the fracture, turn the bandage around the neck, and under the bones, and under the patient's clothes; and twist it from both sides, and when you see that the splint aligns with the fracture, and you clearly see that the stick does not move over the broken bone, then hold it in place each day, and when the swelling subsides, tighten it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under his armpit to raise the shoulder; align the fracture by adjusting the shoulder with the arm tied to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident occurs, up to 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then apply the splint, if necessary, and hold it in place until it is restored; and it is restored in up to 28 days, and less in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It does not happen that the broken or large shoulder joint heals by itself, and it should be neither moved nor forced except by touch; if it is prepared according to the shape of the fracture, and aligned according to its natural form in all ways possible; then apply powder from the mill with abundant egg and light starch, and place two layers of cloth over it; then place a broad and thin stick, slightly larger than the shoulder, under which are woven fine starch strips of linen, so that the stick fits evenly; and then bind it firmly all around, so that the stick does not move from its place, and observe the splint every day; whenever it softens, bind it again, and make sure the stick remains in place if it moves out of its place, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is completed, release it, and be careful, for it is not the bone that easily comes loose.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes before and not beneath the skin, lift it up, remove it, and do as we have said in the treatment of an abscess to cool it.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture by the wound
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The limb is sometimes fractured in the middle, but it happens seldom; however, it often breaks at the extremity. And when it is fractured internally, it sinks downwards, causing the patient great pain, lack of nourishment, and fever, and immediately vomits blood, and the pores open in the fractured bones, and it feels very bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back over his chest, and one places a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two ribcages in your hands, and carefully align it in all ways that you can; until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then place pressure bandages and padding on top of the broken bone, or a lighter splint, and wrap it in one cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move; then turn the limb roundabout, and hold it straight, and tighten the bandage hourly, and if it swells, tighten the bandage; and if it needs to be dislocated, due to corrosion or itching at the site, or pain or abscess, hurry and dislocate it, remove the padding, and address whatever has come from the wound in ways of treatment; then remove the padding, and hold it straight until it heals.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breakage of ribs occurs only in large bones near the back and chest, and they do not bend easily except for when they are slippery; and this is felt clearly at the site of the injury.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the resetting is that you set it evenly, as necessary. Then apply a splint, and tie it with a strap, if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inside, causing the patient severe pain and shortness of breath, as well as coughing like in pleurisy, for the bone pierces the lung; and the patient points to the place where it hurts, and immediately vomits a large amount of blood, this is a serious illness, and they used to apply great effort in the past.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that distend the belly, in order to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not let hot irons come, unless they have arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If they have arrived, we heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And it was said by some that they put leeches on the wound to draw pus, which seems reasonable; however, there is doubt whether the leech draws excess fluids to the wound due to its weak constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And it was said by some that one should cover the wound with damp linen soaked in hot oil and put plasters between the ribs to make the wound evenly healed, then it is cured with a cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels intense pain that he cannot bear through the bone which does not break the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, it is necessary to make an incision on the side of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put one instrument inside for support; then it should be cut, pulled gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound, if they are large, and dress with ointment until it heals. And when pus comes, place dampened linen soaked in rose oil on top, and place it there; cure the area affected by the abscess while the rib heals, and lie down on the side where it should be, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	There is never a break in the collarbone or spine bones, and it does not bend in the same way as others.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, take notice if their hands are softened, swollen, and dead, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. Know that in many positions, he is mortal. And if he is silent and feels well when you hold and prick him, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If such a thing happens to the spine in the back, and you want to know if it will be healthy or not, take notice if the feet are softened, and if there is an accident which is in the hands, and the back suddenly jumps and spasms involuntarily; and when it is put on its stomach, it still jumps involuntarily. And when it is put on its back and wants to sit, it cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this accident does not happen to him, it will be a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward [the patient] if there is an abscess that burns hot, you place on it rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is soothed; then put on one of the soothing and drying ointments and tie it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone is dislocated, it must be covered; and cut the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, then treat it with an ointment healing charcoal until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "head of the cow," you push your thumb of your left hand into it, and make it equal to your right hand in power, then put the ointment and the cloth on it, if you have any need for it; then bind it, and if there is a dislocated bone, you should make it fit, and cut it and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break in the shinbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it occurs, there is only a little lessening at the head; it becomes long, bends towards the outside, and causes pain and swelling at the break.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above [the break], so that you are above the fracture; and feel which is the fracture and the shape of it; and if the fracture is only at the head, then make the fracture equal to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or bends inside, then lay the patient on his stomach so that the restoration of the fracture may be apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, place the plaster on it, then place a splint of wood or horn over the break and hold the fracture still so that it does not move; and apply the yoke under the ribs, until the sides are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on the unaffected side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess swells up, do not touch it until the swelling has subsided, and place what was previously mentioned on it; then return to treatment, and hold it as necessary, if there is no harmful accident; and this is how it is done.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder blade is the part between the back and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two ways: Of which one is that you take a rod made of thick paste, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the rod with two cords and raise it above, and position the patient on one side; then he lets the broken arm hang down over the rod until it reaches the same level as the other shoulder, and make a hump in the rod at this point; then suspend a heavy object or the assistant stretches the other end of the rod below; then the master places the broken part even with his hands together, so that the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is to place the patient on his side and tie his arm to his neck, then command two assistants that one holds the broken part with his hands above, and the other holds the rod below with one cord and extends each part to its own side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the extraction is more forceful, hold one ligature beneath the break and another above it, and extend each of the assistants to their respective parts. And if the break is near the shoulder's head, you must place a moderate ligature beneath the pressure and one towards the side, beneath the break; similarly, if the break is towards the side, you must place a light ligature without labor, as long as the break is equal on the level and on the side. Then make the break equal, as required, and hold it, provided there are no abscesses nearby.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If abscesses are present, do not hold the ligature for more than 7 days, and place a soft cloth soaked in rose oil over it to calm the abscesses; then hold the ligature, and the method of holding is that you place the pliers on the break, then assemble the arm above the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or the chest. Place the gauze, and hold the ligature above the shoulder and above the arm, so that the arm is in a straight position, unless anything prevents it, or the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use splints and place a larger and stronger splint above the break, with at least two fingers of space between each splint, and have each splint be as wide as it passes the break by four fingers on each side. Then hold the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, firmly but not too far apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the abscess of the joint and the swelling, as we have said, while you are restoring the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is hot, leave it to heal until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at it every three days to ensure that pus does not swell or come to the place, or new matter cannot reach the member because it is too narrow. If the pus drains, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such incident occurs, do not remove the splint for less than four days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back and have his hands on his stomach; and place a linen bandage evenly under the affected joint and observe the movement of the broken member every hour of the day or night to ensure that the splint does not move or become soft; then treat with medicine according to its nature, giving it food as before mentioned, so that the food is initially coarse; and when it begins to heal, it should become thick. It is customary for the splint and the leg to be restored in forty days; then remove the splint and administer oil baths and medicines to clean the wound. If the incision is ugly and infected, wait one day or two months to remove it.
de la brisure du bras	of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of 2 bones, which are called the "two shinbones." One is small, and it forms the elbow; the other is large, and it is beneath, toward the little finger. Sometimes only the large one breaks, or sometimes both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small shinbone is broken, restoration and healing are easy; but when the large one is broken, healing is difficult, and it is more painful than when both break together. If only the small shinbone is broken, you must stretch it slightly and make it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large shinbone that is broken, you must stretch it more forcefully; extend it on one log, and raise the elbow of the hand higher than the others, and the smaller finger lower than the others, and cross the patient over himself, placing a log in front of him higher than the patient does not suffer any labor. Then extend the attendant's arm to the part beneath his hand or to the elbow, and one attendant at one side and another on the other above. And then place the patient straight, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there is a fracture in pieces, put each one in its place; and if any of them has slipped out, pricks the keyhole, and you cannot restore it to its place, then saw through and remove the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture in pieces, I have spoken of it in the specific chapter; take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if upon the beginning of the restoration, abscesses arise, apply one cloth made of rosier oil and white beeswax, which should neither be too hard nor too soft; and sew one cloth subtly, until the abscess has been soothed. Then remove the rosier oil and put the paste made from the powder of the mill with egg, afterwards place the sticks, and the stick from the fracture should be more prominent, and a little larger than the others; and know that it must have 7 sticks or more in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone, or two. Hold the fracture higher than other parts, and at all times less in alignment, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter; and may the cloths that are above the fracture be soft and moist, not hard nor harsh; and may the threads, by which it is held, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And observe the member and the ligament afterwards after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accidents happen to the member, such as prurit that happens to the member, then you must irrigate the member with hot water until the prurit is alleviated; and let the member not rest. Then resume the bandaging, and if the ligaments are damaged and the bones dislocated, and similar things, advise accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the urine cannot reach the member because it is too narrow, so that it does not pass through, then you must soften it with a poultice for a short time, and leave it like this for some days until the urine flows through, and then bandage it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not undress him for up to 20 days. Or around this time, he should hold his hands at his neck and make them even, and avoid movement and displacement, and sleep on his back; and know that this break will be restored in 30 or 40 days, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	In the back of the hand and fingers, there are few fractures, but rather many bending multiple times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is fractured or bent, the patient should lie crosswise and rest straight in front of him equally; then place his hand on a cloth extended, and the attendant extends the broken bones, and aligns the mirrors so they are equal, until they are well joined; and apply the poultice and compresses, unless an abscess forms there, then place a splint according to the severity of the fracture; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is near the ventral side of the lower limb, make a tourniquet of cloths, and instruct the patient to tighten it around their fractured limb; then tighten a long cloth, and let it be as thick as the palm of the hand, and tighten, as required.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, it is necessary to place a splint above and another below in the limb, so that the hand is straightened and bound tightly, then bind it all around the hand, and stop the flow between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture occurs in any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, make it straight as required; bind it with the palm, and if you see that it needs a splint to lift the fracture and not move; and if the fracture is in other fingers such as the index or others, make them straight, and bind them with the adjacent healthy finger. Or tie all of them together in one place, for moving is harmful, or put a splint on it, as with a thumb; take care in the restoration and the setting of the abscess and be careful to treat those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The leg bones are often broken, and one sees it when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one places one splint above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each assistant extends their splint to their equal portion; and this is when the break has been set in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the break is near the root of the leg, one splint goes towards the ankle and the others go below the break. And similarly, if it is near the knee, then the splints are below the knee and the extension is above; then the assistant holds the bone equal to their two hands, according to its natural shape, and then applies the plaster and bandage, as long as no abscess comes.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that is hot, let it cool first, then return to your work and treatment; the remedy is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must bind the leg above the break, double a bandage thick for two or three layers, and let the excess remain, then turn the leg until the heels come to the root of the groin, and insert one long pin between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the head of the pin up; then turn the leg and thigh over the bandage, then put the splints on top, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then use linen cloth soft to hold the strain evenly, then begin to bind four or five times on the splint; and as you go higher up the splint, loosen the strain; then attend to the two pins that you inserted between the leg and thigh, and bind four splints that are above, then return down to the head of the pin, until you see under the foot; strap it, so it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, so no abscess or swelling or similar thing comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens, unbind and correct what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are bone pieces that protrude, they must be cut, if possible; and if not, the place must be broken and drained, and treated as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thighbone is broken in such a way that splints are placed there, as in the shoulder or arm; however, in the healing process, this does not cause discomfort to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thighbone is healed within a few days or a little more or less, according to the variations of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the knee joint there is little breakage, but it bends frequently. And if it breaks, it is not a complete break, but rather a crack or fracture, and it causes pain at all places, and without place, and this is felt very much.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when one equalizes the limb that is dislocated with its opposite, as long as it can be assembled in movement; then put the splint, and place a round peg if necessary, and tighten it as needed, then reposition all the alignments that we have said in other breaks, such as abscesses and others; place at each accident what is required, as long as it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "shin" and the other "tibia"; and it happens similarly when the arm breaks, and for this reason the restoration is equal to that of the arm, and the operations are all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	If the slender bone is broken, it bends forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	If the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen; then it bends downwards. Then apply reduction, make it equal, and tie the ends equally; but if the break is misaligned or there are many pieces, the reduction should be less and lighter; align it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two pieces of splints that span the leg on both sides and are as long as from the knee to below; then wrap them in two layers, one above and one below, and tie them in the middle as well, so that the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should apply a splint of wood along the length of the leg, but rather a bandage, and place the leg for preventing movement, and carefully make this at the break where there is pain; and move the leg every day, to see if there is an abscess or other accident; treat it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the break of the bones from the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no break, but sometimes breaks occur in the bones of the foot and toes, and it requires certain treatment in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see the bones rising against each other, put the patient lying on his back with his foot raised, as if he were walking, then place your hand under where the bones are raised, press them back to their places; then cover it with plaster and wool and place a small table with two even surfaces beneath the belly of the foot, then tie the foot in place with bandages and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandages, for you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two bones are broken, restore them as we have said for the bones in the hand; then place a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and let it be slightly larger, then place under the bone that table I mentioned, and hold it securely; and if there are 2 or more, or more, break each bone and place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and hold the bone under the skin; and let the table be positioned above the belly of the bone, so that it touches well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And do not forget the other things I have said about broken bones, after we have discussed them; and treat each case according to its circumstances.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone in the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the female body is broken, make her sit with her legs apart, then incline her to the part of the back and hold her from behind; then fill the hollow with cotton and put in as much as one stone; then turn her over and lower the buttock little by little, and the cotton will leap out at the entrance of the bone, and the bone will come back with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or more: the break will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of barley, tie one end of a cord to it, and push the whole bladder into the bone; then blow hard in the cord so that the bladder inflates inside: the break will return; then fill with cotton, and leave it like this for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the arm of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the bone of the thigh; and these breaks should not be concealed from him who applies his study and practice to them, and read my book. For the breaks indicate various positions for the restoration: therefore follow this instruction.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In a staff when it is broken, take an owl's gullet and put the staff in it; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for three days or more, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	for the one who has a breakage with wound, particularly if it is large, such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or something similar, that it should be treated now, so that the sores mentioned previously bear witness to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, apply vinegar to it, if you have none else, then begin again to heal the breakage in that same hour, or on that day, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess comes up, wait until the ninth day for it to be soothed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad incident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears exposed on the edge of the wound, you must set it gently in place with light pressure and extend it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions do not appear equal for you to set in place, then use this instrument that is made of iron, which is 7 or 8 inches long and the width is according to the size of the wound; therefore, the mirror must grasp 3 or 4 fingers, depending on what is needed for each bone-setting treatment; and it should be round and somewhat large but not too thin so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and it should be sharp in front and thick from the middle forward, as follows:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche," therefore the curved head of the bone should be placed on top of the apparent bone; push it once until it returns to its place and ensure it is equal on both sides. If the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone well, then you must cut the head of the bone so that the instrument can take hold of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, within your power; then remove what remains sharp and in small fragments from the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone has been reset and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. Do as much as you can to make it in its proper place, then moisten one clean linen cloth with black stiptic wine and apply it directly if it's warm; do not put any greased cloth or other substance on the wound where there is oil because it will bring corruption and pus. Then administer splints when you have restored the bone, leave the wound open, cover the surrounding area according to the size of the wound, but be careful that the wound is not constricted with fracture; and many times this has been done by foolish surgeons, causing the patient to become ill, injured, or even die. And the bindings should be softer and more flexible than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is large or bad, and you fear that a mishap may come to it, as we have said, and you feel pain at the place, do not put splints on it; instead, wrap it without using splints, using hard cloth and bind it. And when after one day or two, the bow appears to be swollen at the wound, remove what you had put on it and apply healing ointments such as tetraformula and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, once in the morning and once in the evening, as long as it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be aligned in such a manner that the bone moves down gently but gradually.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it passes many days and cannot heal but the bone keeps moving, since there are small pieces of bone, which is why you should press the wound with pressure, and remove all those dislocated pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula or any other form of corruption appears, it should be treated according to what is mentioned in the chapter above. And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, like the bones of the shin or shoulder, and similar large members, do not draw it out, since many times death may come, but let it stay as long as possible; perhaps it will heal by itself after 20 or 30 days. Then treat the wound if you can; if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The coming sores on the sore (translated as: 'the sores that come upon a sore')
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	There are often times after the fracturing of health that it occurs again, especially near the joint, and it is a displeasing sight to see the figure of the limb; and by chance the limbs cannot perform their natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the limb is fresh: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocola, acacia, and similar ones, so that you take any of these things or all together, and crush them with a sharp liquid such as vinegar or egg white or oil; then apply it to the knot in poultices, and keep it tightly wrapped and not loosen it for many days; and then dislocate it, and begin another, until the swelling subsides; or you may hold it on a piece of wood well-made because the properties of wood are such that they remove all inflammations from the limbs; and if the nodule has already become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut the top off, and reveal the superfluous part; or you may shave it with a razor, until it is removed, and cure it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb which is weak after being set (or treated)
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and remains weak and tender after that, it happens for many reasons: one is when it was bound too tightly and was not bound as it should have been; or when there were too many splints, and the nutrients could not reach the member; or due to excessive rubbing; or due to excessive movements, not at the appropriate time; or because there is little blood in the body, so it remains weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body become strong, until the blood multiplies within him; then administer baths, and give joy and pleasure; afterwards put ointment on the member, so that the ointment attracts great nutrients to it, and rub it frequently with cold water, until the nutrients reach the member; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The member twisted out of health [or order] after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is disfigured, it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and great harm comes from it, and sometimes death; however, if the dislocation and torture are fresh, then they must be treated with hot water or softening herbs such as vismalve leaves, roots, medick, and similar things; and you should make a soothing poultice, such as dittany well made, and take musk from vismalve, mix it with beeswax or camphor oil, and apply the poultice; or you may use figs softened with wheat bran, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the dislocation is removed by rubbing continuously and persistently with moist hands. Movement should be brought to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is grown and hardened, as stone, and needs to be cut with iron, it should be covered up to the bone, at the incision made subtly and gently; and put on a cushion and bandage in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it must now be reset without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the joint swells, and in case it is reset at that point, it should not be moved until it has subsided; for many times it brings pus and other pain.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Whenever this occurs, let the patient be purified, then leave him, until the abscesses have subsided; then immerse the affected limb in hot water and oil, then gently move it, and treat each member as appropriate once it is in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on shoulder dislocations from head to feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It often happens that the jawbones are dislocated on both sides, and dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are slightly dislodged from their places and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the cheek, and saliva drools out of the mouth that it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and it wraps its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a small dislocation returns with various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, you must reset it quickly, without delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the minister holds the patient's head and places one hand of his in the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other hand should be spread apart, to make them even; and command the patient to soften, their jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror set even again, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the jawbones are dislocated, anoint them with hot water and oil, gently adjusting them until they are set; do not force it to return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	When they are set evenly, and the mouth of the patient closes properly, apply a soft cloth soaked in a paste made from rose oil and wax, then gently tie it with fine linen strings.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on his back, and place his head between two pillows, so that it does not move to either side, nor force itself, but take light meat, until the pain is removed, and the jawbones are healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then, if he wants to eat lightly, do not force him to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jawbone is properly knit and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be properly set within an hour and are not returned to their places, then fever and accustomed sweats occur, and possibly rupture of the stomach, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is lost causes; and many times the person who experiences it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	Of the collarbone
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The collarbone cannot dislocate towards the chest and ribs from the inside, nor can it dislocate outwards; however, it sometimes does dislocate, which is felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is as follows: The patient lies on his back and extends his arms. Then he presses firmly against the collarbone with your palm, and it will return. Then place a splint and bandage on it and hold it in place;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	The head of the shoulder that is towards the costal area cannot dislocate; if it does, and if it can be reset to its original position as we have said, then place a splint and bandage on it and hold it in place. Command the patient to rest until he is well.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And likewise, the head of the spine is reset when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	The dislocation of the shoulder   (from the previous sentence)
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder can dislocate in only four ways: one is when it dislocates to the lower part of the socket; and the second is to the part of the pelvis; and by chance, it can dislocate to the upper part, but this rarely happens.
